Do False Testimony or Killing the Killer Negate the Right to Retaliation? Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute on whether actions like false testimony of forgiveness or killing the killer remove the right to qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that qisas is not lost by false testimony of forgiveness or by killing the killer, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the nature of qisas as non-valued property.

Core Idea
Since qisas is not valued property (muttaqawwim), it cannot be guaranteed (lost) by actions that would compensate property.

The passage concludes with a specific dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i. The question is: if false testimony is given that the guardian forgave retaliation, or if the killer is killed by a third party, does the guardian lose the right to qisas? The Hanafis say no, because qisas is not a valuable property (muttaqawwim) and has no equivalent in form or meaning. This lesson unpacks that argument and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis hold that retaliation (qisas) is not guaranteed (i.e., lost) to the guardian by false testimony of forgiveness or by killing the killer. The right to qisas remains.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i (likely) holds that such actions do cause the loss of the right to qisas, presumably because the right to qisas can be compensated or is lost by estoppel.
The passage does not give the Shafi'i dalil, but it is implied.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is that qisas is not 'muttaqawwim' (valued property). It is a personal right of like-for-like, not a commodity. Therefore, it does not have an equivalent (mithl) in form or meaning. Actions that would guarantee a property right (like false testimony or death of the wrongdoer) do not affect qisas.
Key phrase: 'qisas is not valued (muttaqawwim), so it has no equivalent neither in form nor meaning'.
4
Apply to the two scenarios
Scenario 1: False testimony that the guardian forgave qisas. Since qisas is not property, the guardian is not bound by false testimony. Scenario 2: The killer is killed by another. The original right to qisas persists because the killer's death does not extinguish the right (the right is against the killer's estate? Actually, the passage implies the guardian can still claim qisas from the killer's estate? But standard Hanafi: the right to qisas attaches to the killer's person; if he dies, qisas is not possible, so diya may be due. But the passage says 'retaliation is not guaranteed... by killing the killer', meaning the guardian does not lose the right? This is a nuanced point. In the passage, it says: 'retaliation is not guaranteed to the guardian by false testimony on forgiveness, or by killing the killer'. This likely means that these events do not automatically transform the right into diya or extinguish it; rather, the right to qisas remains in theory, but if the killer is dead, qisas cannot be executed, so it effectively converts to diya? The text says 'blood money is only legislated to protect blood from being wasted'. So if the killer is dead, qisas is impossible, so diya becomes due. But the Shafi'i might hold that the guardian loses the right to anything? Hard to tell. We'll stick to the text: the Hanafis say qisas is not guaranteed (i.e., not converted to a compensatory right) by mere false testimony or the killer's death at the hands of another; rather, the right to qisas remains until it is actually impossible (e.g., death of the killer by natural causes). The practical difference is that if the killer is killed by another, the Hanafis may hold that the guardian retains a claim for qisas against the killer's estate? Actually, qisas is a physical punishment on the living body; if the killer is dead, qisas cannot be enforced. So the Hanafi position likely means that the guardian's right to qisas is not automatically replaced by diya as a penalty on the false testifier or the second killer; the guardian is still entitled to qisas from the original killer if possible, but if the killer is dead, then diya is due from his estate. The Shafi'i might hold that these actions create a direct right to diya from the actor. The thamarah (practical consequence) is as given in the toolbox.
This step requires careful reading of the text: 'retaliation is not guaranteed... by killing the killer'.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
If false testimony proves that the guardian forgave qisas, Hanafi holds the right remains, so the killer can be retaliated. Shafi'i presumably holds the guardian is estopped and must take diya. Similarly, if the killer is killed by another, Hanafi holds the original right persists, so the killer's estate may be liable for qisas (or diya). Shafi'i might hold that the guardian's right is lost or converted.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, a like-for-like punishment. In this context, it is not considered valued property (muttaqawwim).
متقوم (muttaqawwim): Valued property that has a recognized monetary value in Shariah.
شهادة باطلة (shahada batila): False testimony, a witness statement that is untrue.
ولي (wali): Guardian, the legal representative of the victim entitled to demand qisas.

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why does false testimony of forgiveness not nullify the right to retaliation?
A) Because false testimony is always invalid.
B) Because qisas is not valued property (muttaqawwim) and thus cannot be lost by such testimony.
C) Because the guardian must forgive in person.
D) Because the killer has a right to a fair trial.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the right to retaliation is not a property right; it cannot be lost by false testimony or the killer's death at the hands of another; diya is only a fallback when qisas is truly impossible.

8 min
Invalidity of Qiyas Based on a Distinguishing Description
Stating a usul rule on invalid qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a qiyas is invalid because it relies on a description that distinguishes the branch from the original, and apply this principle to evaluate analogies.

Core Idea
A qiyas that depends on a distinguishing description between asl and far' is invalid.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Usul introduces a critical condition for valid qiyas: the illah must be shared without differentiation. The author warns that if the analogy requires a description that separates the branch from the original, the qiyas fails. Let's unpack this principle and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The author states that any qiyas that can only be established by a description that creates a distinction between the original (asl) and branch (far') is invalid.
2
Understand the rationale
Why does this invalidate? Because qiyas requires a common cause (illah) equally present in both cases. If the description differentiates, then the illah is not truly common.
3
Apply to the example
The author gives an example: wealth can become obligatory by condition in exchange for non-wealth, and a slave can be sold for more than its value by mutual consent, but not by aggression. This shows that some rules are based on mutual consent, not on inherent value; analogies based on value distinctions may be invalid.
The example illustrates how a description (consent vs. aggression) distinguishes the ruling.
4
Distinguish from valid qiyas
Note that this does not invalidate all qiyas; only those where the distinguishing feature is the sole basis for the analogy. If there is a common illah despite other differences, the qiyas may be valid.
The key is to identify whether the distinguishing description is the basis or incidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ألا يُرى أن المال يجب بالشرط مقابلاً بغير مال، ويجوز بيع عبد قيمته ألف بألوف، فيثبت الفضل بالتراضي، ولا يثبت شيء من ذلك بالعدوان بحال.
وكل قياس لا يقوم إلا بوصف تقع به المفارقة بين الفرع والأصل: باطل على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
وأما القضاء بمثل غير معقول : فهو كغير المال المتقوم إذا ضمن بالمال المتقوم : كان مثلاً غير معقول.
مثل النفس تُضمن بالمال ؛ لأن المال ليس بمثل للنفس، لا صورةً ولا معنى؛ لأن الآدمي مالك مبتذل لما سواه، والمال مملوك مبتذل، فلا يتشابهان بوجه.
ولهذا قلنا: إن المال غير مشروع مثلاً عند احتمال القصاص؛ لأن القصاص مثل الأول صورةً ومعنى، وهو إلى الإحياء الذي هو المقصود أقرب، فلم يجز أن يزاحمه ما ليس بمثل لا صورة ولا معنى.
وإنما شرع عند عدم المثل ؛ صيانة للدم عن الهَدَر، ومِنَّةً على القاتل بأن سَلَمَتْ له نفسه، وللقتيل بأن لم يُهدر حقه.
ولهذا قلنا نحن، خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله : إن القصاص لا يُضمن لوليه بالشهادة الباطلة على العفو، أو بقتل القاتل ؛ لأن القصاص ليس بمتقوم، فلم يكن له مثل لا صورةً ولا معنى.
وإنما شرعت الدية ؛ صيانةً للدم عن الهدر، والعفو عن القصاص مندوب إليه ) ، فكان جائزاً أن يُهدر، بل حَسَناً.
ولهذا قلنا : إن ملك النكاح لا يُضمن بالشهادة بالطلاق بعد الدخول، وبقتل المنكوحة وبردتها ؛ لأنه ليس بمال متقوم، وإنما يقوم بالمال بضع المرأة ؛ تعظيماً لخَطَره ، وإنما الخَطَر للمملوك ، فأما الملك الوارد عليه : فلا، حتى صح إبطاله بغير شهود ولا ولي.
ولهذا لم يُجعل له حكم التقوم عند الزوال، لأنه ليس بتعرض له بالاستيلاء، بل إطلاق له.
ولا يلزمنا الشهادة بالطلاق قبل الدخول، فإنها عند الرجوع توجب ضمان نصف المهر؛ لأن ذلك لم يجب قيمة للبضع.
ألا يُرى أنه لم يجب مهر المثل تاماً كاملاً، كما قال الشافعي، لكن المسمى الواجب بالعقد لا يُستحق تسليمه عند سقوط تسليم البضع، فلما أوجبوا عليه تسليم النصف مع فوات تسليم البضع: كان قصراً ليده عن ذلك المال، فأشبه الغصب.
وأما القضاء الذي في حكم الأداء فمثل رجل تزوج امرأةً على عبد 19 بغير عينه : أنه إذا أدى القيمة : أجبرت على القبول، وقيمة الشيء: قضاء له لا محالة ، وإنما يُصار إليها عند العجز عن تسليم الأصل.
وهذا الأصل لما كان مجهولاً من وجه، ومعلوماً من وجه صح
(۱) قوله : والعفو عن القصاص مندوب إليه : قلت: روى الإمام أبو حنيفة عن عطاء عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن عفا عن دم : لم يكن له ثواب إلا الجنة». أخرجه الحارثي في المسند.
Do you not see that wealth becomes obligatory by condition in exchange for non-wealth, and it is permissible to sell a slave worth one thousand for thousands, so the excess is established by mutual consent, and nothing of that is established by aggression at all. And every qiyas that is only established by a description by which differentiation occurs between the branch and the original is invalid, as we will explain, God willing. As for judgment by a non-rational equivalent: it is like non-valuable property when it is guaranteed by valuable property: it is a non-rational equivalent. For example, life is guaranteed by wealth because wealth is not an equivalent for life, neither in form nor in meaning; because a human being is an owner, utilizing what is other than him, while wealth is owned and utilized, so they are not similar in any way. For this reason, we said: wealth is not prescribed as an equivalent when qisas is possible; because qisas is an equivalent to the first in form and meaning, and it is closer to the revival which is the intended goal, so it is not permissible for what is not an equivalent in form or meaning to compete with it. It is only prescribed when the equivalent is absent; to preserve blood from being wasted, and as a favor upon the killer that his life is spared, and for the killed that his right is not wasted. For this reason, we said, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may God have mercy on him): qisas is not guaranteed to its guardian by false testimony on the pardon, or by killing the killer; because qisas is not valuable property, so it has no equivalent in form or meaning. Blood money was only prescribed to preserve blood from being wasted, and pardon of qisas is recommended, so it was permissible for it to be wasted, rather it is good. For this reason, we said: the right of marriage (milk al-nikah) is not guaranteed by testimony of divorce after consummation, or by killing the wife or her apostasy; because it is not valuable property. Rather, the vagina (bud') is compensated by wealth to magnify its importance, and the importance is for the owned thing. As for the right over it (the marriage right), no; to the point that its annulment is valid without witnesses or guardian. For this reason, it is not given the ruling of value upon dissolution, because it is not about seizure but about release. And we are not obliged by the testimony of divorce before consummation, for it obligates guarantee of half the dower upon retraction; because that is not a value for the vagina. Do you not see that the full equivalent dower (mahr al-mithl) is not obligatory completely, as al-Shafi'i said, but the named dower obligated by the contract is not entitled to be delivered when the delivery of the vagina is lost. So when they obligated him to deliver half with the loss of delivery of the vagina: it was a restriction of his hand from that wealth, so it resembles usurpation. As for the judgment that is in the ruling of performance: it is like a man who marries a woman on a slave not specified: that if he pays its value, she is compelled to accept. And the value of a thing is a judgment (qada') for it necessarily. It is only resorted to when unable to deliver the original. And this original, being unknown in one aspect and known in another, is valid. (1) His statement: 'And pardon of qisas is recommended': I said: Abu Hanifa narrated from 'Ata' from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever pardons blood: he will have no reward except Paradise.' Al-Harithi extracted it in al-Musnad.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul principle that a qiyas (analogy) is invalid if it relies on a description that distinguishes the original (asl) from the branch (far'). The author first gives an illustration: wealth can be obligated by condition in exchange for non-wealth, and a slave's sale can have excess value by mutual consent, but nothing of that is established by aggression. Then the principle is stated clearly. The author then moves to the concept of 'judgment by a non-rational equivalent' (qada' bi mithlin ghayri ma'qul), which occurs when something is compensated by something that is not a true equivalent in form or meaning. The example is blood money (diyah) for life: life is compensated by money, but money is not a rational equivalent because a human is the master and user of property, while property is owned and used—they are not similar. Therefore, in Hanafi fiqh, when qisas (retaliation) is possible, money is not prescribed as a substitute because qisas is the true equivalent in form and meaning, being the taking of life for life, which is closer to the purpose of preservation. Blood money is only prescribed when qisas is absent, as a mercy to prevent bloodshed. The author then presents a dispute with al-Shafi'i: Hanafis say that qisas is not guaranteed to its guardian by false testimony regarding pardon or by killing the killer, because qisas is not property (mutaqawwim) and has no equivalent. Shafi'i apparently holds that it can be guaranteed. Similarly, the right of marriage (milk al-nikah) is not guaranteed by false testimony of divorce or by killing the wife, because it is not valuable property; the compensation for the vagina (bud') by wealth is to honor its significance, not to assign a value to the marital right. This is why marriage can be annulled without witnesses or guardian. The passage then discusses a ruling on dowry: if a man marries a woman on an unspecified slave and later pays its value, the woman must accept, as value is a form of judgment when unable to deliver the original. The footnote provides a hadith about the virtue of pardoning qisas. Throughout, the author argues that many things are not subject to valuation or guarantee because they are not comparable to property in a rational sense.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): An equivalent or similar thing. In qiyas, a true equivalent matches in form and meaning; a non-rational equivalent is a substitute lacking such match.
قياس (qiyas): Legal analogy. This passage sets a condition for validity: the description that is the basis must not distinguish the branch from the original.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes when a qiyas is invalid?
A) When there is any difference between the original and branch.
B) When the qiyas cannot be established without a description that distinguishes the branch from the original.
C) When the qiyas involves a financial transaction.
D) When the qiyas is based on rational reasoning.

Key Takeaway
A qiyas that depends on a distinguishing description between asl and far' is invalid; the illah must be truly common.

intermediate

The Concept of Non-Rational Equivalent: Qisas and Diyah
Explaining the concept of non-rational equivalent with life and diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a rational equivalent (mithl ma'qul) and a non-rational equivalent (mithl ghayr ma'qul) and explain why diyah is not a substitute when qisas is possible.

Core Idea
Money is not a rational equivalent for life; diyah is only a substitute when qisas is unavailable.

The author now introduces the idea of a 'judgment by a non-rational equivalent'. This occurs when something is compensated by something that is not a true match in form or meaning. The prime example is life being compensated by wealth. Understanding this helps clarify why in Hanafi fiqh, when qisas is possible, diyah cannot compete.

Guided Path
1
Define 'rational equivalent' and 'non-rational equivalent'
The text defines a non-rational equivalent as when something is compensated by something that is not a true match in form (surah) or meaning (ma'na). For example, wealth for life is non-rational because a human is an owner/user of property while property is owned/used.
2
Identify the example: life vs. money
The author says: 'life is guaranteed by wealth because wealth is not an equivalent for life, neither in form nor in meaning' and explains the essential difference: humans own and use property, but property is owned and used.
3
Apply to the rule: diyah only when qisas is absent
Since money is not a rational equivalent for life, it cannot compete with qisas (the true equivalent in form and meaning - life for life). Diyah is only prescribed when qisas is impossible, to preserve life from being wasted and as a favor to the killer.
The text says: 'qisas is an equivalent to the first in form and meaning, and it is closer to the revival which is the intended goal, so it is not permissible for what is not an equivalent in form or meaning to compete with it.'
4
Note the wisdom behind diyah
Diyah is a concession: it saves the killer's life and ensures the victim's right is not lost. It is not a substitute of equal standing but a fallback to avoid bloodshed.

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul principle that a qiyas (analogy) is invalid if it relies on a description that distinguishes the original (asl) from the branch (far'). Then the principle is stated clearly. The author then moves to the concept of 'judgment by a non-rational equivalent' (qada' bi mithlin ghayri ma'qul), which occurs when something is compensated by something that is not a true equivalent in form or meaning. The example is blood money (diyah) for life: life is compensated by money, but money is not a rational equivalent because a human is the master and user of property, while property is owned and used—they are not similar. Therefore, in Hanafi fiqh, when qisas (retaliation) is possible, money is not prescribed as a substitute because qisas is the true equivalent in form and meaning, being the taking of life for life, which is closer to the purpose of preservation. Blood money is only prescribed when qisas is absent, as a mercy to prevent bloodshed. The author then presents a dispute with al-Shafi'i: Hanafis say that qisas is not guaranteed to its guardian by false testimony regarding pardon or by killing the killer, because qisas is not property (mutaqawwim) and has no equivalent. Shafi'i apparently holds that it can be guaranteed. Key Terms
مثل (mithl): Equivalent. In this lesson, a rational equivalent matches in form and meaning; a non-rational equivalent does not.
الآدمي مالك مبتذل (al-adami malik mubtadhal): A human is an owner who utilizes property; this is the essential quality that makes humans unlike property, which is owned and utilized.

Why does the passage say money is not a rational equivalent for life?
A) Because life is more valuable than any amount of money.

C) Because the Quran prohibits taking money for life.

Key Takeaway
A rational equivalent matches in form and meaning; money and life do not, thus diyah is only a non-rational substitute when qisas is impossible.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Hanafi Position on Guaranteeing Qisas and Milk al-Nikah
Dispute with Shafi'i on guaranteeing non-property rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that qisas and milk al-nikah are not guaranteed by false testimony or killing, and evaluate the practical difference with al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Qisas and milk al-nikah are not property; thus they cannot be compensated by money.

This passage presents a concrete dispute with al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi school argues that qisas (the right to retaliation) and milk al-nikah (the marital right) are not valuable property (mutaqawwim). Therefore, if someone falsely testifies that the guardian pardoned qisas, or kills the wife, they are not liable to pay compensation. This contrasts with the Shafi'i view, which likely treats them as compensable. Let's examine the reasoning and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim
The author states: 'qisas is not guaranteed to its guardian by false testimony on the pardon, or by killing the killer'. Similarly, 'milk al-nikah is not guaranteed by testimony of divorce after consummation, or by killing the wife or her apostasy'.
2
Understand the basis: not property (mutaqawwim)
The reason is that qisas and milk al-nikah are not valuable property (mal mutaqawwim). They are personal rights that cannot be measured in monetary terms. The text says: 'because qisas is not valuable property, so it has no equivalent in form or meaning'.
This builds on the earlier lesson: money is not a rational equivalent for these rights.
3
Contrast with al-Shafi'i
The author explicitly says 'contrary to al-Shafi'i', implying that Shafi'i holds that qisas can be guaranteed by false testimony. The basis for Shafi'i's view is not given here, but it likely rests on analogizing to property rights.
4
Analyze the exception: divorce before consummation
The author notes that false testimony of divorce before consummation does obligate half the dower. This is not a value for the marital right (bud'), but a consequence of the contract (dower) being lost; it is analogized to usurpation.
This exception shows that the rule applies to the right itself, not to contractual obligations.
5
Apply to milk al-nikah
The right of marriage (milk al-nikah) is not guaranteed even if the wife is killed or apostatizes, because it is not property. The compensation for the vagina (bud') is to honor its importance, not to give it a price.
This further supports the principle that personal rights are not compensable.

ألا يُرى أن المال يجب بالشرط مقابلاً بغير مال، ويجوز بيع عبد قيمته ألف بألوف، فيثبت الفضل بالتراضي، ولا يثبت شيء من ذلك بالعدوان بحال.
وكل قياس لا يقوم إلا بوصف تقع به المفارقة بين الفرع والأصل: باطل على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
وأما القضاء بمثل غير معقول : فهو كغير المال المتقوم إذا ضمن بالمال المتقوم : كان مثلاً غير معقول.
مثل النفس تُضمن بالمال ؛ لأن المال ليس بمثل للنفس، لا صورةً ولا معنى؛ لأن الآدمي مالك مبتذل لما سواه، والمال مملوك مبتذل، فلا يتشابهان بوجه.
ولهذا قلنا: إن المال غير مشروع مثلاً عند احتمال القصاص؛ لأن القصاص مثل الأول صورةً ومعنى، وهو إلى الإحياء الذي هو المقصود أقرب، فلم يجز أن يزاحمه ما ليس بمثل لا صورة ولا معنى.
وإنما شرع عند عدم المثل ؛ صيانة للدم عن الهَدَر، ومِنَّةً على القاتل بأن سَلَمَتْ له نفسه، وللقتيل بأن لم يُهدر حقه.
ولهذا قلنا نحن، خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله : إن القصاص لا يُضمن لوليه بالشهادة الباطلة على العفو، أو بقتل القاتل ؛ لأن القصاص ليس بمتقوم، فلم يكن له مثل لا صورةً ولا معنى.
وإنما شرعت الدية ؛ صيانةً للدم عن الهدر، والعفو عن القصاص مندوب إليه ) ، فكان جائزاً أن يُهدر، بل حَسَناً.
ولهذا قلنا : إن ملك النكاح لا يُضمن بالشهادة بالطلاق بعد الدخول، وبقتل المنكوحة وبردتها ؛ لأنه ليس بمال متقوم، وإنما يقوم بالمال بضع المرأة ؛ تعظيماً لخَطَره ، وإنما الخَطَر للمملوك ، فأما الملك الوارد عليه : فلا، حتى صح إبطاله بغير شهود ولا ولي.
ولهذا لم يُجعل له حكم التقوم عند الزوال، لأنه ليس بتعرض له بالاستيلاء، بل إطلاق له.
ولا يلزمنا الشهادة بالطلاق قبل الدخول، فإنها عند الرجوع توجب ضمان نصف المهر؛ لأن ذلك لم يجب قيمة للبضع.
ألا يُرى أنه لم يجب مهر المثل تاماً كاملاً، كما قال الشافعي، لكن المسمى الواجب بالعقد لا يُستحق تسليمه عند سقوط تسليم البضع، فلما أوجبوا عليه تسليم النصف مع فوات تسليم البضع: كان قصراً ليده عن ذلك المال، فأشبه الغصب.
وأما القضاء الذي في حكم الأداء فمثل رجل تزوج امرأةً على عبد 19 بغير عينه : أنه إذا أدى القيمة : أجبرت على القبول، وقيمة الشيء: قضاء له لا محالة ، وإنما يُصار إليها عند العجز عن تسليم الأصل.
وهذا الأصل لما كان مجهولاً من وجه، ومعلوماً من وجه صح
(۱) قوله : والعفو عن القصاص مندوب إليه : قلت: روى الإمام أبو حنيفة عن عطاء عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن عفا عن دم : لم يكن له ثواب إلا الجنة». أخرجه الحارثي في المسند.
Do you not see that wealth becomes obligatory by condition in exchange for non-wealth, and it is permissible to sell a slave worth one thousand for thousands, so the excess is established by mutual consent, and nothing of that is established by aggression at all. And every qiyas that is only established by a description by which differentiation occurs between the branch and the original is invalid, as we will explain, God willing. As for judgment by a non-rational equivalent: it is like non-valuable property when it is guaranteed by valuable property: it is a non-rational equivalent. For example, life is guaranteed by wealth because wealth is not an equivalent for life, neither in form nor in meaning; because a human being is an owner, utilizing what is other than him, while wealth is owned and utilized, so they are not similar in any way. For this reason, we said: wealth is not prescribed as an equivalent when qisas is possible; because qisas is an equivalent to the first in form and meaning, and it is closer to the revival which is the intended goal, so it is not permissible for what is not an equivalent in form or meaning to compete with it. It is only prescribed when the equivalent is absent; to preserve blood from being wasted, and as a favor upon the killer that his life is spared, and for the killed that his right is not wasted. For this reason, we said, contrary to al-Shafi'i (may God have mercy on him): qisas is not guaranteed to its guardian by false testimony on the pardon, or by killing the killer; because qisas is not valuable property, so it has no equivalent in form or meaning. Blood money was only prescribed to preserve blood from being wasted, and pardon of qisas is recommended, so it was permissible for it to be wasted, rather it is good. For this reason, we said: the right of marriage (milk al-nikah) is not guaranteed by testimony of divorce after consummation, or by killing the wife or her apostasy; because it is not valuable property. Rather, the vagina (bud') is compensated by wealth to magnify its importance, and the importance is for the owned thing. As for the right over it (the marriage right), no; to the point that its annulment is valid without witnesses or guardian. For this reason, it is not given the ruling of value upon dissolution, because it is not about seizure but about release. And we are not obliged by the testimony of divorce before consummation, for it obligates guarantee of half the dower upon retraction; because that is not a value for the vagina. Do you not see that the full equivalent dower (mahr al-mithl) is not obligatory completely, as al-Shafi'i said, but the named dower obligated by the contract is not entitled to be delivered when the delivery of the vagina is lost. So when they obligated him to deliver half with the loss of delivery of the vagina: it was a restriction of his hand from that wealth, so it resembles usurpation. As for the judgment that is in the ruling of performance: it is like a man who marries a woman on a slave not specified: that if he pays its value, she is compelled to accept. And the value of a thing is a judgment (qada') for it necessarily. It is only resorted to when unable to deliver the original. And this original, being unknown in one aspect and known in another, is valid. (1) His statement: 'And pardon of qisas is recommended': I said: Abu Hanifa narrated from 'Ata' from Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever pardons blood: he will have no reward except Paradise.' Al-Harithi extracted it in al-Musnad.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the usul principle that a qiyas (analogy) is invalid if it relies on a description that distinguishes the original (asl) from the branch (far'). The author first gives an illustration: wealth can be obligated by condition in exchange for non-wealth, and a slave's sale can have excess value by mutual consent, but nothing of that is established by aggression. Then the principle is stated clearly. The author then moves to the concept of 'judgment by a non-rational equivalent' (qada' bi mithlin ghayri ma'qul), which occurs when something is compensated by something that is not a true equivalent in form or meaning. The example is blood money (diyah) for life: life is compensated by money, but money is not a rational equivalent because a human is the master and user of property, while property is owned and used—they are not similar. Therefore, in Hanafi fiqh, when qisas (retaliation) is possible, money is not prescribed as a substitute because qisas is the true equivalent in form and meaning, being the taking of life for life, which is closer to the purpose of preservation. Blood money is only prescribed when qisas is absent, as a mercy to prevent bloodshed. The author then presents a dispute with al-Shafi'i: Hanafis say that qisas is not guaranteed to its guardian by false testimony regarding pardon or by killing the killer, because qisas is not property (mutaqawwim) and has no equivalent. Shafi'i apparently holds that it can be guaranteed. Similarly, the right of marriage (milk al-nikah) is not guaranteed by false testimony of divorce or by killing the wife, because it is not valuable property; the compensation for the vagina (bud') by wealth is to honor its significance, not to assign a value to the marital right. This is why marriage can be annulled without witnesses or guardian. The passage then discusses a ruling on dowry: if a man marries a woman on an unspecified slave and later pays its value, the woman must accept, as value is a form of judgment when unable to deliver the original. The footnote provides a hadith about the virtue of pardoning qisas. Throughout, the author argues that many things are not subject to valuation or guarantee because they are not comparable to property in a rational sense.

Key Terms
مثل (mithl): Equivalent. The Hanafi position relies on qisas not having a mithl in form or meaning.
ملك النكاح (milk al-nikah): The right of marriage, i.e., the husband's authority over the marital relationship. Not considered property.
تقوم (taqawwum): Being valuable property that can be compensated. Qisas and milk al-nikah are not mutaqawwim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi, why is a false witness who testifies to pardon of qisas not liable to pay damages?
A) Because the witness can retract his testimony.
B) Because qisas is not property (mutaqawwim) and has no equivalent in form or meaning.
C) Because the guardian still has the option to demand qisas.
D) Because the pardon is not valid if testimony is false.

Key Takeaway
Only property (mal) can be guaranteed; personal rights like qisas and marital rights are not compensable.

When Extension Attaches Corruption: The Hanafi Rule on Prayer Extending into Prohibited Time
Explains ruling when prayer extends into corrupt time and its analogy with unintentional rak'ah addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that corruption attaching after valid initiation is excused, and distinguish it from deliberate initiation in corrupt time.

Core Idea
Corruption attaching to a validly begun prayer is excused; the key is the intention at initiation.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi clarifies a crucial Hanafi usul rule: if an obligation is triggered by a valid cause (sabab), subsequent corruption does not necessarily invalidate the act. The text uses the example of Asr prayer started early and prolonged until sunset, and draws an analogy with the case of unintentionally adding a fifth rak'ah. We will unpack the reasoning and the legal principle behind this dispensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Find Imam Muhammad's explicit ruling for Asr prayer that extends into sunset. The text states that the prayer does not become invalid.
The ruling is a clear exception to the general requirement that the entire prayer must fall within valid time.
2
Locate the Sabab
Identify what triggers the obligation (wujub). Here, the entering of Asr time is the valid cause. The prayer began when the sabab was sound.
The sabab is the time entering, not the completion of prayer.
3
Analyze the Reasoning
The text gives two reasons: (1) the Law allows occupying all the time with performance, and (2) avoiding corruption while engaged in prayer is difficult (muta'addhir). The corruption that attaches to a valid building is excused.
This is a qiyas on building (bina'): if one valid part is laid, later imperfections are overlooked.
4
Examine the Qiyas
The narration about the fifth rak'ah shows that if a person unintentionally stands for an extra rak'ah, it is recommended to complete. The corruption from the extra rak'ah is excused because it was not intentional.
The same logic applies: unintentional or unavoidable corruption is excused.
5
Contrast with Initiation in Corrupt Time
If one deliberately begins prayer when the time is already corrupt (e.g., after sunset), the prayer is invalid because the sabab is corrupt and one can avoid it.
The distinguishing factor is the intention and the ability to avoid corruption at the start.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان ذلك الجزء فاسداً : انتقص الواجب، كالعصر تُستأنف في وقت الاحمرار ، فإذا غربت الشمس وهو فيها : لم يتغير، ولم تفسد. ولا يلزم إذا ابتدأ العصر في أول الوقت، ثم مده إلى أن غربت الشمس قبل فراغه منها فإنه نص محمد أنه لا تفسد، وقد كان الوجوب مضافاً إلى سبب صحيح. ووجهه أن الشرع جعل الوقت متّسعاً ، ولكن جعل له حق شغل كل الوقت بالأداء، فإذا شغله بالأداء : جاز وإن اتصل به الفساد ؛ لأن ما يتصل به من الفساد بالبناء: جعل عفواً ؛ لأن الاحتراز عنه مع الإقبال على الصلاة متعذر. وقد روى هشام عن محمد رحمهما الله فيمن قام إلى الخامسة في العصر : أنه يستحب له الإتمام؛ لأنه من غير قصده ثبت، فإذا اتصل به الفساد : صار في الحكم عفواً ، فصار بمنزلة المؤدى في وقت الصحة. بخلاف حالة الابتداء ؛ لأنه بقصده ثبت الفساد، إذ الاحتراز عنه ممكن، بأن يختار وقتاً لا فساد فيه.
And if that part is corrupt: the obligatory act is diminished, like Asr prayer begun at the time of redness [of sunset], then when the sun sets while he is in it: it does not change and does not become invalid. And it is not necessary [to invalidate] if he begins Asr at the beginning of the time, then prolongs it until the sun sets before he completes it, for indeed Imam Muhammad ruled that it does not become invalid, and the obligation was attached to a valid cause. And its reasoning is that the Law has made the time expansive, but has given it the right to occupy all the time with performance, so if he occupies it with performance, it is permissible even if corruption attaches to it; because the corruption that attaches to it due to building [upon the valid part] is deemed excused, because avoiding it while being engaged in prayer is difficult. And Hisham narrated from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, regarding one who stood for a fifth [rak'ah] in Asr: that it is recommended for him to complete, because it occurred without his intention; then when corruption attaches to it, it becomes in the ruling excused, so it becomes like that performed in a valid time. Contrary to the case of beginning, because by his intention corruption is established, since avoiding it is possible by choosing a time without corruption.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage discusses a key usul principle regarding the relationship between obligation (wujub) and time. The author explains that if a person begins the Asr prayer in a valid time (before the sun turns red) and prolongs it until sunset, the prayer remains valid according to Imam Muhammad's explicit ruling. The reasoning is that the obligation was attached to a valid cause (the beginning of the time), and the law allows occupying the entire time with performance. Any corruption that attaches later due to the passage of time is excused because avoiding it while engaged in prayer is difficult. The narration from Hisham reinforces this: if someone mistakenly stands for a fifth rak'ah in Asr, it is recommended to complete, because the extra rak'ah was not intended. The corruption from the extra rak'ah is excused due to the difficulty of avoidance. However, this leniency applies only if the corrupt act occurs after valid initiation; if one deliberately begins in a corrupt time, it is invalid because one can choose a valid time.

Key Terms
فساد (fasad): Corruption or invalidity of the act due to time or extra elements.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation attached to a cause (sabab) that triggers performance.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation, here the time entering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if someone begins Asr prayer at the beginning of its time and prolongs it until sunset without completing it?
A) The prayer is invalid because part of it occurred in prohibited time.
B) The prayer is valid because the obligation was attached to a valid cause and extension is excused.
C) The prayer must be repeated as qada.
D) The prayer becomes voluntary (nafl) after sunset.

Key Takeaway
If a valid cause triggers obligation, subsequent corruption due to difficulty of avoidance is excused; the initiation intention is key.

Causation Transfer When Time Is Empty of Performance
Explains ruling when time passes without any performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that when a time-bound obligation is completely missed, the obligation attaches to the entire time, requiring perfect qada without deficiency.

Core Idea
No performance in a time-bound obligation reverts causation to the whole time, demanding full perfection in qada.

This passage from Al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul presents a key distinction: if you start a prayer in its time but do not complete it, causation transfers to the valid part; but if you never perform it at all, the original rule holds—the whole time is the cause. This impacts how you must make up the missed prayer, requiring full conditions and not a deficient substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text contrasts two cases: when time contains partial performance (previous case) and when it is completely empty (this case). Note the shift in the causation rule.
The 'previous case' is referenced but not included in this passage.
2
Understand the necessity (darura)
When there is performance, necessity demands transferring causation from the whole time to a part to allow validity. Without any performance, this necessity disappears.
Necessity is the key driver of the altered rule (istihsan).
3
Apply the original rule
With no necessity, the original principle applies: the entire time period is the cause (sabab) for the obligation.
Original rule: 'كل الوقت سبباً' – the whole time is the cause.
4
Derive the consequence for qada
Since the obligation is attached to the whole time, it must be performed with full perfection (proper conditions, not deficiently).
You cannot perform the qada in a shortened or incomplete manner.
5
Note the exception
The author rejects a hypothetical exception: a disbeliever who accepts Islam at the last moment of Asr, then forgets and remembers later, cannot perform Asr at the time of redness because this is not narrated (i.e., not supported by transmitted sources).
This shows that new obligations (fresh after Islam) are treated differently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا خلا الوقت عن الأداء أصلاً : فقد ذهبت الضرورة الداعية إلى نقل السببية عن الكل إلى الجزء، وهو ما ذكرنا من شغل الأداء، فانتقل الحكم إلى ما هو الأصل، وهو أن يُجعل كل الوقت سبباً، فإذا فاتت العصر أصلاً أضيف وجوبها إلى جملة الوقت، دون الجزء الفاسد، فوجبت بصفة الكمال، فلم يجز أداؤها بصفة النقصان. ولا يلزم إذا أسلم الكافرُ في آخر وقت العصر، ثم لم يُؤدِّ حتى احمرَّت الشمس في اليوم الثاني، وقد نسي، ثم تذكرها، فأراد أن يؤديها عند احمرار الشمس؛ لأن هذا لا يُروى.
And as for when the time is completely empty of performance: then the necessity that called for transferring causation from the whole to the part has disappeared, which is the aforementioned occupation with performance. So the ruling reverts to the original, which is that the whole time is made the cause. So if the Asr prayer is lost entirely, its obligation is attached to the entire time, not to the corrupt part, so it is obligatory with full description, and it is not permissible to perform it deficiently. And it is not necessary [to apply this] if a disbeliever embraces Islam at the end of the time for Asr, then does not perform it until the sun becomes red the next day, having forgotten, then remembers and wants to perform it at the time of redness; because this is not narrated.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents a contrasting scenario: when the entire time passes without any performance of the prayer (e.g., the person did not pray Asr at all), the rule changes. In the previous case, because the person did begin praying, the obligation was attached to the valid part of time. But here, since the time is devoid of any performance, there is no necessity to transfer causation from the whole time to a part. Instead, the obligation attaches to the entire time period, meaning the prayer must be performed in a complete, perfect form (qada with full conditions). The author then addresses a hypothetical: if a disbeliever accepts Islam at the very end of Asr time, then forgets and does not pray until the next day at the time of redness, can he pray Asr then? The author says this case is not narrated (i.e., no transmitted ruling), implying it is not analogous because the disbeliever's Islam causes a fresh obligation.

Key Terms
سببية (sababiyya): The quality of being a cause (sabab) for obligation.
فوات (fawat): Loss of the obligation due to time passing without performance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a person completely misses Asr prayer (does not start it at all in its time), how is the obligation attached?
A) To a part of the time, allowing deficient performance.
B) To the entire time, requiring perfect performance.
C) The obligation becomes null and void since the time passed.
D) The prayer can be performed in any subsequent time as nafl.

Key Takeaway
When a time-bound obligation is completely unperformed, the whole time period is the cause, demanding a perfect qada without deficiency.

Hajj: Constrained or Expanded Obligation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of Hajj obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether Hajj is mudayyaq or musawwa', and EXPLAIN their respective analogies.

Core Idea
Hajj's obligation is expanded over a lifetime, not constrained to the first year.

This passage addresses a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: once Hajj becomes obligatory, must it be performed in the first available year? Abu Yusuf compares the first year's Hajj months to prayer time, making it immediate; Muhammad compares it to a lifetime, allowing delay. The resolution hinges on a broader usul principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine what makes Hajj 'problematic' according to the text: is the first year a determined time for performance?
The disagreement is about the first year's status, not about validity if delayed.
2
State the agreement
Both imams agree that if one delays beyond the first year, the Hajj is validly performed (adā').
3
Contrast the positions
Abu Yusuf: the first year's months are like prayer time, so delay is sinful (mudayyaq). Muhammad: the entire life is the time, so delay is permissible (musawwa').
Key difference: nature of the timeframe.
4
Examine the analogies
Abu Yusuf analogizes to prayer which has specific windows; Muhammad analogizes to making up Ramadan (qada) which can be done anytime on the day.
The analogies reflect different conceptions of the obligation's temporal scope.
5
Note the tarjih
The relied-upon position is Muhammad's: an absolute command does not necessitate fawr, so Hajj is expanded (musawwa').
This tarjih is based on the general usul principle discussed in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النوع الرابع من المؤقتة فهو المشكل منه وهو حج الإسلام، ومعنى قولنا إنه مشكل: أن وقته العمر، وأشهر الحج في كل عام صالح لأدائه، أم أشهر الحج من العام الأول وقت متعين لأدائه؟ ولا خلاف في الوصف الأول، حتى إذا أخر عن العام الأول: كان مؤدياً. فأما الوصف الثاني : فهو صحيح عند أبي يوسف رحمه الله في الله في الحال، وأشهر الحج في هذا العام الذي لَحِقَه الخطاب به : بمنزلة وقت الصلاة، فإذا أدرك العام الثاني : صار ذلك بمنزلة العام الأول، لا يصير كذلك إلا بشرط الإدراك. وقال محمد رحمه الله : بل لا يتعين هذا الوقت للأداء، وإنما وقته العمر، فيسعُه التأخيرُ بشرط أن لا يفوته عن العمر. هذا وأشهر الحج من العام بمنزلة يوم أدركه في حق قضاء رمضان، وإنما يُعرف بأن الحج يجب مضيقاً أو موسعاً : فقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : مضيَّقاً، لا يسع فيه التأخيرُ عن العام الأول. وقال محمد رحمه الله : يجب موسعاً يسع تأخيره عن العام الأول. وقال الكرخي وجماعةٌ من مشايخنا رحمهم الله تعالى : إن هذا إلى أن الأمر المطلَقُ عن الوقت أيوجب الفور، أم لا؟ مثل وجوب الزكاة وصدقة الفطر والعُشر والنذر بالصدقة المطلقة. فقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله : على الفور. وقال محمد رحمه الله : على التراخي، فكذلك الحج، فأما تعين الوقت : فلا. والذي عليه عامة مشايخنا رحمهم الله تعالى: أن الأمر المطلق لا يوجب الفور.
As for the fourth type of time-bound obligations, it is the problematic one, which is Hajj of Islam. The meaning of our saying it is problematic: that its time is a lifetime, and the months of Hajj in every year are suitable for its performance, but are the months of Hajj from the first year a determined time for its performance? There is no disagreement on the first description: if he delays beyond the first year, he has performed it (validly). As for the second description: it is correct according to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) immediately, and the months of Hajj in this year that the address reached him are like the time of prayer. So when he reaches the second year, that becomes like the first year, but only with the condition of reaching it. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: No, this time is not determined for performance; rather its time is the lifetime, so delay is permissible on condition that he does not miss it within his lifetime. This and the months of Hajj from the year are like the day he reaches in the matter of making up Ramadan. It is known whether Hajj is obligatory as constrained (mudayyaq) or expanded (musawwa'): Abu Yusuf said: constrained, delay beyond the first year is not allowed. Muhammad said: it is obligatory as expanded, delay beyond the first year is allowed. Al-Karkhi and a group of our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said: This goes back to whether an absolute command without time necessitates immediate (fawr) or not? Like the obligation of zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and vows of absolute charity. Abu Yusuf said: immediate. Muhammad said: delay (tarakhi), and so Hajj. As for determination of time: no. The general view of our scholars is that an absolute command does not necessitate immediate.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the obligation of Hajj. The issue is whether the first year after becoming capable is a determined time (mutta'ayyin) for Hajj or not. Abu Yusuf holds that the first year's months of Hajj are like the time of prayer: immediate obligation, and if delayed, one must perform it the next year, but the delay is sinful because the time is 'constrained' (mudayyaq). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the time of Hajj is the entire lifetime (al-'umr), so delaying is permissible as long as it is performed before death; the first year is not determined, making it 'expanded' (musawwa'). Al-Karkhi and others link this to the general usul principle: does an absolute command (amr mutlaq) imply immediacy (fawr) or delay (tarakhi)? Abu Yusuf says fawr, Muhammad says tarakhi. However, the relied-upon position (according to 'amma mashayikhina) is that an absolute command does not necessitate fawr, thus the view of Muhammad is adopted. Note: This discussion is unique to Hajj because its time is the entire life, unlike prayer which has specific windows.

Key Terms
فور (fawr): Immediacy: an obligation must be performed at the earliest possible time.
تراخي (tarakhi): Delay: an obligation can be performed at any time within the overall timeline.
مضيق (mudayyaq): Constrained: the time is so limited that delay is not allowed.
موسع (musawwa'): Expanded: the time is broad enough to allow delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on delaying Hajj beyond the first year?
A) Sinful
B) Permissible
C) Invalidates Hajj
D) Requires a sacrifice

Key Takeaway
Hajj is obligatory expanded (musawwa'), not constrained (mudayyaq), so delay within one's lifetime is permissible without sin.

Does an Absolute Command Imply Immediate Execution?
Usul principle: fawr vs tarakhi for absolute commands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi position that an absolute command (amr mutlaq) does not necessitate fawr, and APPLY this principle to other obligations like zakat and sadaqat al-fitr.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, an absolute command does not imply fawr.

This passage expands the Hajj dispute to a foundational usul question: what does an absolute command without a time specification require? The majority of Hanafi scholars (al-Karkhi and others) resolve that the command itself does not demand immediacy. This principle governs many obligations beyond Hajj, such as zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, and absolute vows.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text asks: does an absolute command (amr mutlaq) necessitate immediate execution (fawr)? This applies to all obligations formulated as absolute commands.
The principle is stated explicitly: 'al-amr al-mutlaq la yujibu al-fawr'.
2
Note the disagreement
Abu Yusuf holds that an absolute command does require fawr; Muhammad holds that it does not.
This disagreement mirrors the Hajj dispute.
3
Understand the basis
The disagreement stems from different interpretations of the nature of the command: fawr proponents see the command as requiring an immediate response; tarakhi proponents see it as a general permission to act within the feasible time.
No specific textual evidence is cited; it's a difference in usul methodology.
4
Recognize the tarjih
The majority ('amma mashayikhina) adopt Muhammad's view: no fawr.
This is the mufta bihi for all absolute commands.
5
Apply to other cases
The same ruling applies to zakat, sadaqat al-fitr, 'ushr, and absolute vows: delay is permissible within the feasible time without sin.
But note that many of these have their own time limits (e.g., zakat after a year); the principle applies when no time is specified.

Source Text

The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that an absolute command does not require immediate execution; this applies to Hajj, zakat, and other absolute obligations.

Effect of Prohibition on Contracts: Mudadah
Usul rule: effect of prohibition on contracts based on mudadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of mudadah to determine whether a prohibition invalidates a contract.

Core Idea
A prohibition voids a contract only if it contradicts the contract's essential nature.

This passage explores a key usul principle: why does a prohibited marriage become void while a prohibited sale remains valid? The answer lies in the concept of mudadah (contradiction). Marriage is inherently tied to permissibility, so prohibition negates its essence. Sale, however, concerns ownership of substance, which can exist even with prohibition. Understanding this distinction is essential for applying prohibitions correctly in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contracts and the prohibition
The passage contrasts marriage (nikah) and sale (bay') when a prohibition applies. Note that in both cases, the prohibition is assumed (e.g., marriage without witnesses, sale of wine).
The prohibition here is not from the contract itself but from external factors.
2
Analyze the essential nature of each contract
Marriage is legislated for 'necessary ownership' (milk daruri) inseparable from permissibility. Sale is for ownership of the substance (milk al-'ayn), where permissibility is subsidiary.
This distinction is based on the primary objective of each contract.
3
Apply the rule of mudadah
If the prohibition contradicts the essential nature, the contract becomes void (batil). For marriage, prohibition contradicts the essence (permissibility of intimacy), so the contract is void. For sale, prohibition does not contradict the essence (ownership of substance), so the contract may remain valid but tainted.
Mudadah means direct opposition: the prohibition negates the very purpose of the contract.
4
Test with examples from the text
The passage gives examples: sale of wine, Magian slave-girl, beasts – these are prohibited but ownership transfers. Marriage cannot be legislated with prohibition because its purpose is inherently halal.
These examples illustrate that sale can exist in a 'place of prohibition' (mawdi' al-hurma).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما سقط الحد، وثبت النسبُ والعِدَّة؛ لشبهة العقد، ولأن النكاح شرع لملك ضروري لا ينفصل عن الحِل، حتى لم يُشرع مع الحرمة. ومن قضية النهي: التحريم، فبطل العقد؛ لمضادة ثبتت بمقتضى النهي، بخلاف البيع؛ لأنه وضع لملك العين، والتحريم لا يضاده؛ لأن الحل فيه تابع. ألا يُرى أنه شرع في موضع الحُرمة، وفيما لا يحتمل الحل أصلاً، كالأمة المجوسية والعبيد والبهائم، وكملك الخمر.
And the [hadd] penalty is dropped, but lineage and 'iddah are established due to the semblance of a contract; because marriage is legislated for necessary ownership inseparable from permissibility, such that it is not legislated with prohibition. And from the consequence of prohibition is unlawfulness, so the contract becomes void due to a contradiction established by the requirement of the prohibition, unlike sale; because it is established for ownership of the substance, and prohibition does not contradict it, because permissibility in it is subsidiary. Do you not see that it is legislated in a place of prohibition, and in what does not admit permissibility at all, like the Magian slave-girl, male slaves, and beasts, and like ownership of wine.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of prohibition (nahy) on contracts. In a marriage contract performed without witnesses (as previously discussed), the hadd penalty for zina is dropped due to the semblance of a contract, but lineage and 'iddah are established. The reason marriage is void when prohibited is that marriage is inherently tied to permissibility (halal) of sexual relations; prohibition contradicts its essential nature. In contrast, sale contracts are for ownership of property ('ayn), which can exist even if the object is prohibited (like wine or a Magian slave-girl). Permissibility in sale is subsidiary, not inherent. Hence, a prohibited sale is not automatically void; it may be tainted but can still transfer ownership in some cases.

Key Terms
المضادة (al-mudadah): Contradiction between the prohibition and the essential nature of the contract
ملك العين (milk al-'ayn): Ownership of the substance, the primary objective in sale contracts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a prohibited marriage become void while a prohibited sale does not?
A) Because sale has more conditions.
B) Because permissibility is inherent to marriage but subsidiary to sale.
C) Because prohibition is weaker in sale.
D) Because marriage requires a guardian.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule of mudadah: a prohibition voids a contract only if it contradicts the contract's essential nature.

Qiyas: Extension of Rulings from Original to Branch
States the principle of qiyas: ruling extends from original to branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of qiyas and apply it by identifying the original, branch, and cause in an example.

Core Idea
A substitute takes the ruling of the original solely through their shared legal cause.

This passage introduces a cornerstone of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the principle that a ruling applicable to an original case (asl) extends to its peripheral branches (furu') through a shared legal cause ('illa). The author uses the classic example of tayammum with dust substituting for wudu with water to illustrate how the purifying quality of water serves as the cause, making dust a valid substitute. Understanding this principle is essential for grasping how Hanafi scholars derive rulings for new situations via analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The passage states that a ruling 'extends from it (the original) to its branches and to its causes.' Recognize that 'it' refers to the original case (asl) with an established ruling.
2
Understand 'Substitution'
The text says 'what acts in place of another: it acts by the cause of the original.' Grasp that when something substitutes for the original, it does not create a new ruling; rather, it inherits the ruling because of the shared cause.
3
Analyze the Example
The author cites tayammum (dust) substituting for water in wudu. Identify the original (water), the substitute (dust), and the shared cause (purification). Confirm that the ruling of purification applies to both.
Do you see (alā tara) signals a logical illustration.
4
Extract the Qiyas Structure
Formally, this is qiyas jali (clear analogy): Asl = wudu with water, Hukm al-asl = purification is achieved, Far' = tayammum with dust, 'Illah = purification (taharah). The ruling extends from asl to far' because of the shared illah.
5
Apply the Principle
Now consider another Hanafi scenario: when a person cannot stand, prayer is offered sitting. Identify the original (standing prayer), the branch (sitting prayer), and the cause (the obligation of prayer itself). The ruling of obligation extends.
This is a typical usul exercise to reinforce the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يتعدى منه إلى أطرافه، ويتعدى إلى أسبابه، وما يعمل بقيامه مقام غيره: فإنما يعمل بعلة الأصل. ألا يُرى أن التراب لما قام مقامَ الماء: نظر إلى كون الماء مطهراً،
Then it extends from it to its branches, and extends to its causes, and what acts in place of another: it acts by the cause of the original. Do you not see that when dust (tayammum) takes the place of water: it is considered [that] water is purifying,
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage introduces a principle of qiyas (analogical reasoning). A legal ruling that applies to an original case (asl) extends to its peripheral cases (atraf) and to its causes (asbab). When something substitutes for another (like tayammum substituting for wudu with water), it takes the ruling of the original based on the underlying cause ('illa). The example given is tayammum with pure dust: it functions as a purifier because water is purifying; the 'illa of purification is common. This is a fundamental usul principle for extending rulings.

Key Terms
يتعدى (yata'adda): extends, transfers from one case to another
علة (illa): legal cause or ratio legis

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what basis does tayammum with dust take the ruling of wudu with water?
A) Because dust is also a liquid.
B) Because the cause of purification is shared.
C) Because the Prophet did tayammum.
D) Because water is not available.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas extends a ruling from an original to a substitute based on a shared legal cause ('illa), not on superficial similarity.

The Khiyar al-Shart Analogy: Connecting Naskh and Khusus in Hanafi Usul
Ruling on khiyar al-shart from al-Ziyadat with analogy to naskh and khusus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the analogy between khiyar al-shart and daliil al-naskh to explain why specification of the option and price is required, and identify the conditions for a valid sale with option in one item.

Core Idea
Khiyar al-shart affects the cause like naskh, and the ruling like istithna—specification saves the sale.

This passage combines a specific fiqh ruling from al-Ziyadat with a deep usul insight: the option of condition (khiyar al-shart) is structurally analogous to proof of abrogation (daliil al-naskh) in its effect on the cause, and to exception (istithna) in its effect on the ruling. Understanding this analogy sharpens your ability to see how Hanafi usul uses qiyas not only for rulings but also for analyzing the structure of legal causes. You will learn the exact conditions that make a sale with khiyar al-shart valid and why ambiguity invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and items
A man sells two slaves for a total price, stipulating an option in one. What must he specify? The passage says: specify which slave has the option and its portion of the price.
This is the core condition.
2
Understand the effect of khiyar al-shart
The option does not prevent the formation of the contract (entry into offer) but prevents it from becoming binding. That is why it is analogous to naskh in cause and istithna in ruling.
The phrase 'لا يمنع الدخول في الإيجاب، ويمنع الدخول في الحكم' is key.
3
Apply the analogy to daliil al-khusus
Just as specification (khusus) saves a general text from being overbroad, specification of the option and price saves the sale from invalidity.
The analogy is drawn explicitly in the text.
4
Distinguish from the free/slave case
In selling a free man and a slave together, the condition is inherently corrupt because the free man is not a valid object of sale. That case invalidates the whole contract, unlike khiyar al-shart where specification can cure.
The contrast shows how the nature of the defect determines whether specification can cure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دليل النسخ. ونظير دليل الخصوص: مسألة خيار الشرط. وس [؟] يعين قال في «الزيادات»: في رجل باع عبدين بألف درهم على أنه بالخيار ويسمي ثمنه في أحدهما: إن البيع لا يصح حتى يُعين الذي فيه الخيار، فأما إذا أجمل الثمن، ولم يُعيّن الذي فيه الخيار، أو عين أحدهما ولم الآخر: لم يجز البيع؛ لأن الخيار لا يمنع الدخول في الإيجاب، ويمنع الدخول في الحكم، فصار في السبب: نظير دليل النسخ، وفي الحكم نظير الاستثناء، فقيل: لا بدَّ من إعلام الثمن والمبيع؛ لجواز البيع، بمنزلة الحر والعبد، وإذا وجد التعيين، وإعلام الحصة: صح البيع، ولم يُعتبر الذي شرط فيه الخيار شرطاً فاسداً في الآخر. بخلاف الحر والعبد، وما شاكل ذلك في قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه يعتبر شرطاً فاسداً في الآخر، لا محالة، فيفسد به البيع، والله أعلم.
Proof of abrogation. And an analogue to the proof of specification: the issue of the option of condition. It was said: in al-Ziyadat: concerning a man who sold two slaves for a thousand dirhams on the condition that he has the option and he specifies the price for one of them: the sale is not valid until he specifies which one has the option. As for if he made the price ambiguous and did not specify which one has the option, or he specified one but not the other: the sale is not permissible; because the option does not prevent entry into the offer, but prevents entry into the binding effect. So it became in cause: an analogue to the proof of abrogation, and in ruling an analogue to exception. So it was said: it is necessary to specify the price and the sold item for the permissibility of the sale, like the case of a free man and a slave. And if specification and informing of the portion occur, the sale is valid, and the condition stipulated in one is not considered a corrupt condition regarding the other. Contrary to the free man and slave and similar cases, in the view of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he considers it a corrupt condition regarding the other, necessarily, so the sale becomes invalid due to it. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Ziyadat (one of the six core books of Imam Muhammad) illustrating an usul principle: the analogy between daliil al-naskh (proof of abrogation) and daliil al-khusus (proof of specification). The specific fiqh example is khiyar al-shart (option of condition) in a sale of two slaves. The ruling: if a man sells two slaves for a total price, stipulating an option for himself in one of them, he must specify which slave the option applies to and allocate a portion of the price to it. If he does not specify, the sale is invalid. The reasoning is that khiyar al-shart prevents the sale from becoming binding (luzum) but does not prevent the initial offer (ijab). Thus, it resembles naskh in that it affects the cause (sabab) and istithna' in that it affects the ruling (hukm). The passage also compares this to the case of selling a free man and a slave together, which is invalid because the free man cannot be sold. Abu Hanifa's view is that in the free/slave case, the condition is corrupt and invalidates the sale. However, in the khiyar al-shart case, specification saves the sale. The key condition is specification of the item with the option and its price portion.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract allowing a party to rescind within a specified period.
دليل النسخ (daliil al-naskh): A proof that indicates the abrogation of a previous ruling by a later one.
دليل الخصوص (daliil al-khusus): A proof that specifies a general ruling to a particular case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a man sells two slaves with a condition of option in one of them, what must he specify for the sale to be valid?
A) The price of each slave equally
B) Which slave has the option and its portion of the price
C) The total price only
D) The names of both slaves

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart in a multi-item sale requires specification of the option item and its price portion to avoid invalidity, reflecting a structural analogy to naskh and istithna in Hanafi usul.

Order of Mention as an Indicator for Tarjih
Explaining how order of mention indicates precedence in tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that order of mention indicates precedence for tarjih, using the analogy from Sa'i to wills.

Core Idea
Order of mention signals strength and justifies tarjih, even without explicit command.

In Hanafi usul, the sequence in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed actions can itself carry legal weight. This passage explains how the order in Sa'i (the ritual walking) became obligatory due to the Prophet's practice, not the Quranic text. The same reasoning extends to wills: the order in which a testator lists bequests indicates priority. Understanding this principle helps us see how indirect indicators can guide preference in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Claim
The passage claims that 'precedence in mention indicates the strength of the preceded one' and that this is suitable for tarjih (preference). Restate this in your own words.
Focus on the relationship between order and strength.
2
Locate the Evidence
The evidence for this claim is the Prophet's action in performing Sa'i in a specific order. The text says this order became obligatory 'by his action, not by the text of the verse.' Identify what type of dalil this is (e.g., Sunnah fi'liyyah).
The Quranic verse does not prescribe the order; the Prophet's practice does.
3
Understand the Qiyas
The text draws an analogy from Sa'i to wills: as the Prophet's order in Sa'i indicates priority, so does the testator's order in listing bequests. Identify the asl (original case), far' (new case), and illa (effective cause).
The illa is 'indication of strength of concern'.
4
Recognize the Usul Principle
Extract the general usul rule: when a text or action presents items in a sequence, the order can be used to assign priority in tarjih. This is a secondary indicator, not a primary command.
This principle helps resolve conflicts between evidences or rulings.
5
Apply the Principle
Consider a new scenario: a hadith lists 'ablution' then 'prayer'. What does the order imply? How would a Hanafi scholar use it?
The order suggests that the first-mentioned item has greater weight in that context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير أن السعي لا ينفك عن ترتيب والتقديم في الذكر يدل على قوة المقدَّم ظاهراً، وهذا يصلح للترجيح، فترجح به، فصار الترتيب واجباً بفعله، لا بنص الآية. وهذا كما قال أصحابنا رحمهم الله في الوصايا بالقُرب النوافل: إنه يبدأ بما بدأ به الميت؛ لأن ذلك دلالة على قوة الاهتمام، فصلح للترجيح.
However, the Sa'i is not free from order, and precedence in mention indicates the strength of the preceded one apparently, and this is suitable for tarjih (preference), so it is preferred by it, thus order became obligatory by his action, not by the text of the verse. And this is as our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said concerning wills for supererogatory acts of worship: that one begins with what the deceased began with; because that is an indication of the strength of concern, so it is suitable for tarjih.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage deals with the usul principle that the order of mention in a text can be used to indicate precedence and thus serve as a basis for tarjih (preference) when there is a conflict. The author gives the example of performing Sa'i during Hajj, where the order is considered obligatory not because the Quranic verse explicitly commands it, but because the Prophet's action (the order he followed) indicates the importance of the sequence. The author then supports this with an analogy from Hanafi fiqh concerning wills: when a person bequeaths multiple supererogatory acts of worship, the executor should start with what the deceased mentioned first, as that shows the testator's priority. This reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) from the Sa'i case. The logical chain is: the Prophet's action implies a preference; this preference is sufficient to make order obligatory in similar cases.

Key Terms
ترجيح (tarjīḥ): Preferring one evidence or ruling over another based on a valid indicator.
التقديم في الذكر (al-taqdīm fī al-dhikr): The precedence given to an item by mentioning it before others in a single utterance or text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the order of Sa'i considered obligatory?
A) Because the Quranic verse commands it.
B) Because the Prophet's action established it.
C) Because the Sahaba agreed on it.
D) Because it is mentioned first in the verse.

Key Takeaway
Order of mention is a valid indicator for tarjih in Hanafi usul, deriving its authority from the Prophet's action and analogical reasoning.

Extending Ruling via Dalalah: The Case of the Forgetful Fasting Person
Deriving the ruling for intercourse from eating/drinking via dalaalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of dalalah to extend a ruling from a specific text to an analogous case by identifying the 'illah and rebutting objections based on prevalence.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness is a natural trait; the same 'illah applies to all acts, so the ruling extends from eating to intercourse.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul illustrates how the Hanafi school moves from a specific textual ruling to a broader application using dalalah (indication). The hadith excuses the forgetful fasting person who eats or drinks; the question is whether this extends to other acts like intercourse. By identifying the underlying cause ('illah) as forgetfulness being a natural disposition, the school derives that any forgetful act during fasting carries the same ruling—no penalty and no make-up. The text also anticipates and refutes an objection based on the differing prevalence of these acts, strengthening the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text and its ruling
Locate the hadith: 'Whoever forgets while fasting and eats or drinks, let him complete his fast, for Allah fed him and gave him drink.' The ruling is that the fast remains valid and no compensation is required.
This is a specific text (nass) about eating and drinking.
2
Extract the 'illah from the base text
The text does not state the reason explicitly. From the phrase 'for Allah fed him and gave him drink,' the Hanafi scholars infer that the excuse is forgetfulness itself, which is a natural, involuntary trait (samaawi). The act is attributed to Allah, not to the person.
This extraction is called takhrij al-manat.
3
Apply the 'illah to the new case
If forgetfulness is the cause, it applies to any act performed forgetfully during fasting, including intercourse. The same 'illah produces the same ruling: no invalidation and no qada'.
This is qiyas jaliy (explicit analogy) via dalalah.
4
Address the counterargument about prevalence
An objector argues that forgetfulness in eating/drinking is common due to fasting's necessity, while forgetfulness in intercourse is rare, so the analogy fails. The Hanafi response balances two factors: incentive (cause of inclination) and inherent force (the desire's natural strength). Eating/drinking has high incentive but low inherent force; intercourse has low incentive but high inherent force. They are equivalent, so the 'illah remains valid.
This refines the 'illah by showing it is not based on frequency but on the nature of forgetfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك : أن النص في عذر الناسي (۱) وَرَدَ في الأكل والشرب، وثبت حكمه في الوطء دلالةً ؛ لأن النسيان فعل معلوم بصورته ومعناه، أما صورته فظاهرة، وأما معناه أنه مدفوع إليه خلقةً وطبيعة، فكان ذلك سماوياً محضاً، فأضيف إلى صاحب الحق، فصار عفواً. هذا معنى النسيان في نظيره. لغة، وهو كونه مطبوعاً عليه، فعملنا بهذا المعنى فإن قيل: هما متفاوتان؛ لأن النسيان يغلب في الأكل والشرب؛ لأن الصومَ يُحوجه إلى ذلك، ولا يُحوجه إلى المواقعة، بل يُضعفه عنها، فصار كالنسيان في الصلاة لم يُجعل عذراً؛ لأنه نادر. قلنا : للأكل والشرب مزية في أسباب الدعوة ، وفيه قصور في حاله؛ لأنه لا يغلب البشر، وأما المواقعة فقاصرة في أسباب الدعوة ولكنها كاملة في حالها، لأن هذه الشهوة تغلب البشر ، فصارا سواء، فصح الاستدلال.
And from that: The text regarding the excuse of the forgetful person came regarding eating and drinking, and its ruling was established for intercourse by indication; because forgetfulness is an action known by its form and meaning. As for its form, it is apparent; as for its meaning, it is that [the person] is driven to it by creation and nature, so that is purely heavenly, so it is attributed to the Owner of the right, and thus it becomes forgiven. This is the meaning of forgetfulness in its analog. Linguistically, it is being naturally disposed to it, so we acted upon this meaning. If it is said: They are different because forgetfulness prevails in eating and drinking because fasting necessitates that, and it does not necessitate intercourse, but rather weakens one from it, so it becomes like forgetfulness in prayer, not made an excuse because it is rare. We say: Eating and drinking have an advantage in the causes of inclination, but there is deficiency in their state because they do not overcome human nature. As for intercourse, it is deficient in the causes of inclination but complete in its state because this desire overcomes human nature. So they become equal, and the deduction is valid.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of extending a ruling via dalaalah (indication) based on the underlying meaning. The ruling for the forgetful fasting person (no penalty for eating/drinking) is extended to intercourse because the effective cause ('illah) is forgetfulness as a natural trait, not the specific act. The objection that the acts differ in prevalence is refuted by analyzing the balance of incentive and inherent force: eating/drinking has stronger external incentive but weaker internal compulsion, while intercourse has weaker external incentive but stronger internal compulsion, making them equivalent in terms of the excuse. This is a classic qiyas jaliy (explicit analogy).

Key Terms
النص (al-nass): A clear textual statement from Quran or Sunnah
دلالة (dalalah): Indication; deriving a ruling from a text by understanding its underlying meaning ('illah)
النسيان (al-nisyan): Forgetfulness as a natural disposition, not a deliberate act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is forgetfulness considered a valid excuse (not penalized)?
A) Because it is unintentional and therefore not sinful
B) Because it is a natural trait (samaawi) that attributes the act to Allah
C) Because the person can make up the fast later
D) Because the act is rare and thus overlooked

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of dalalah allows extending a ruling from a specific text to analogous cases by extracting a general 'illah from the text's inherent meaning, even when the new case is not explicitly mentioned.
