Dispute on the 'Illah for Qisas: Wound vs. Destruction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the 'illah for qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the effective cause ('illah) for qisas and apply the principle of kamil (completeness) vs. naqis (deficiency) to derive the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
The 'illah for qisas is the wound that breaks the structure, not mere lethality.

The hadith 'No qisas except with the sword' appears to limit retribution to sword killings. But Hanafi usul requires identifying the effective cause ('illah) underlying the text. This passage presents a classic intra-madhhab debate: Abu Hanifa defines the 'illah as a wound that breaks the bodily structure (zahir and batin), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue it is any act the body cannot bear, even without a wound. The resolution hinges on the principle that the complete act (kamil) is the basis, not the deficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key text
The hadith 'لا قود إلا بالسيف' is the basis. Analyze its apparent meaning and the intended act (striking with the sword).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
2
Extract the legal issue
The act has an intended meaning (ma'na): the injury by wounding. The ruling (qisas) is built on equivalence in injury.
The 'illah must be derived from this meaning.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa says the 'illah is the wound that breaks the structure outwardly and inwardly (e.g., a sword cut).
He emphasizes the completeness of the act in breaking the body.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the 'illah is what the body cannot bear, causing death, whether wounded or not (e.g., crushed by a large stone).
They focus on the outcome (death) and deterrence.
5
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
He uses the principle that the complete act (kamil) is the original (asl); the deficient (naqis) cannot be the basis, especially when doubts avert punishment.
The Sahibayn's view that the body is a mere means is rejected as a delusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «لا قَوَدَ إلا بالسيف» وأراد به الضرب بالسيف، ولهذا الفعل معنى مقصود، وهو الجناية بالجرح، وما يُشبهه، والحكم جزاء يُبتنى على المماثلة في الجناية، وكان ثابتاً بذلك المعنى. واختلف فيه، فقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : ذلك المعنى هو الجرح الذي ينقض البنية ظاهراً وباطناً. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : معناه ما لا تطيق البنية احتماله ، فتهلك جرحاً كان أو لم يكن حتى قالا: يجب القود بالقتل بالحجر العظيم؛ لأنا نعلم أن القصاص وجب عقوبةً وزجراً عن انتهاك حرمة الأنفس، وصيانة حياتها، وانتهاك حرمتها بما لا تطيق حمله، ولا تبقى معه، فأما الجَرحُ على البدن: فلا عبرة به، إنما البدن وسيلة، فما يقوم بغير وسيلة : كان أكمل. عن هذا أن معنى الجناية هو: ما لا تطيق النفس احتماله، لكن الأصل في كل فعل هو الكمال، والنقصان بالعوارض، فلا يُجعل الناقص أصلاً ، بل الكاملُ يُجعل أصلاً، ثم يتعدى حكمه إلى الناقص إن كان من جنس ما يثبت بالشبهات، فأما أن يُجعل الناقص أصلاً خصوصاً فيما يُدرأ بالشبهات : فلا. وها هنا الكامل فيما قلنا ما ينقض البنية ظاهراً وباطناً هو الكامل في النقض على مقابلة كمال الوجود. وقولهما : إن البدن وسيلةٌ : وَهَمٌ وغَلَطٌ
And from that: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'No qisas except with the sword' and he intended by it striking with the sword, and this act has an intended meaning, which is the injury by wounding and what resembles it, and the ruling is a recompense built on equivalence in the injury, and it was established by that meaning. And they differed concerning it: Abu Hanifa said: that meaning is the wound that breaks the structure outwardly and inwardly. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: its meaning is what the structure cannot bear, so it perishes whether it was a wound or not, so much so that they said: qisas is obligatory for killing with a great stone; because we know that qisas was obligated as a punishment and deterrence from violating the sanctity of lives, and protecting their lives, and violating their sanctity by what they cannot bear, and they cannot survive with it. As for wounding the body, no consideration is given to it; the body is only a means, so what exists without a means is more complete. About this, the meaning of injury is: what the soul cannot bear. But the principle in every action is completeness, and deficiency is by accidents, so the deficient cannot be made the original, rather the complete is made the original, then its ruling extends to the deficient if it is of the kind that is established by doubts. But to make the deficient the original, especially in matters that are averted by doubts, is not allowed. And here the complete in what we said—that which breaks the structure outwardly and inwardly—is the complete in breaking in return for the completeness of existence. And their statement that the body is a means is a delusion and error.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the effective cause ('illah) for qisas (retributive justice) based on the hadith 'لا قود إلا بالسيف'. Abu Hanifa argues that the 'illah is a wound that visibly and internally breaks the bodily structure (like a sword cut). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the 'illah is any act that the body cannot bear and causes death, even without a wound (e.g., dropping a large stone). Abu Hanifa's response uses the principle of kamil (completeness) and naqis (deficiency): the complete act (wounding that breaks structure) is taken as the original, and the deficient act (without wound) is only included if it falls under the same category. He refutes the Sahibayn's claim that the body is merely a means, asserting that the wound is directly the subject of injury.

Key Terms
القود (al-qawad): Qisas, retributive justice for killing or wounding
الجناية (al-jinayah): The act of aggression causing harm to the body
المعنى (al-ma'na): The effective cause ('illah) for the legal ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa in this passage, what is the required condition for qisas?
A) The act must be committed with a sword
B) The act must cause a wound that breaks the bodily structure
C) The act must be one that the body cannot bear
D) The act must involve a tool made of iron

Key Takeaway
The 'illah for qisas is the wound breaking the structure, not mere lethality, based on the principle that the complete act is the original.

Analogical Dispute: Applying Hadd al-Zina to Liwat
Dispute within Hanafi school on qiyas for hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on applying hadd al-zina to liwat via qiyas, and evaluate the arguments of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn using the principle of completeness of cause.

Core Idea
Analogy to hudud requires completeness of cause; a deficient act cannot be analogized to a complete one.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the application of the hadd punishment for zina (adultery) to the act of liwat (sodomy). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that the effective cause of zina exists in liwat even more intensely, so the hadd applies. Abu Hanifa counters that liwat is deficient in key aspects such as progeny destruction and mutual desire, making analogy invalid in hudud. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi usul principle that hudud are averted by shubuhat and require strict, complete analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State what the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule regarding liwat, and what Abu Hanifa rules.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Sahibayn apply hadd, Abu Hanifa applies ta'zir.
2
Extract the effective cause (ma'na) proposed by the Sahibayn
Identify the core meaning they claim to be common: fulfillment of desire by ejaculation in a prohibited orifice. Note how they argue this meaning is stronger in liwat.
They rely on dalalat al-nass (textual indication) to argue that the meaning of zina linguistically encompasses liwat.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Understand why he rejects the analogy: the complete effective cause of hadd in zina includes destruction of progeny (the child is legally destroyed) and mutual desire. Liwat is deficient because it only wastes sperm and lacks natural mutual desire.
The response also argues that in hudud, the complete form is the basis; analogy from complete to deficient is invalid.
4
Apply the usul principle of hudud
Note the principle that hudud are averted by shubuhat (suspicions). Therefore, strict qiyas is not allowed when the analogy is incomplete.
This is a key Hanafi maxim: hudud are based on the most complete and certain grounds.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: Sahibayn would impose hadd (stoning/flogging) for liwat, while Abu Hanifa would impose ta'zir (discretionary punishment).
This illustrates how a difference in usul leads to a difference in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أيضاً أن أبا يوسف ومحمداً رحمهما الله أوجبا حد الزنا باللواطة بدلالة النص ؛ لأن الزنا : اسم لفعل معلوم، ومعناه معلوم، وهو قضاء الشهوة بسفح الماء في محل محرَّم مشتهى، وهذا المعنى بعينه موجود في اللواطة وزيادة؛ لأنه في الحرمة فوقه، وفي سفح الماء فوقه، وفي الشهوة مثله، وهذا معنى الزنا لغةً. والجواب عن هذا : أن الكامل أصل في كل باب، خصوصاً في الحدود، والكامل في سفح الماء : ما يُهلك البشر حكماً ، وهو الزنا؛ لأن ولد الزنا هالك حكماً ؛ لعدم مَن يقوم بمصالحه، فأما تضييع الماء: فقاصر؛ لأنه قد يَحِلُّ بالعَزل، ولا يُفسد الفراش، وكذلك الزنا كامل بحاله؛ لأنه غالب الوجود بالشهوة الداعية من الطرفين، وأما هذا الفعل فقاصر بحاله ؛ لأن الداعي إليه شهوة الفاعل فأما صاحبه فليس في طبعه داع إليه، بل الطبع مانع، ففسد الاستدلال بالكامل على القاصر في حكم يُدرأ بالشبهات. والترجيح بالحرمة : باطل ؛ لأن الحرمة المجردة بدون هذه المعاني: غير معتبرة لإيجاب الحد ، ألا يُرى أن شرب البول : لا يوجب الحدَّ كمال الحرمة.
And from that also is that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad made obligatory the hadd of zina for liwat by textual indication; because zina is a name for a known act, and its meaning is known: it is the fulfillment of desire by pouring water (sperm) in a forbidden, desired place. And this very meaning exists in liwat and more; because in prohibition it is above it, in pouring water it is above it, and in desire it is like it. And this is the linguistic meaning of zina. The answer to this: that the complete is the basis in every chapter, especially in hudud. And the complete in pouring water is what destroys progeny legally, which is zina, because the child of zina is legally destroyed due to lack of one to manage his interests. As for wasting water, it is deficient because it can be made permissible by withdrawal, and it does not ruin the lineage. And similarly, zina is complete in its state because it typically occurs with desire from both parties. As for this act (liwat), it is deficient in its state because the desire is only from the doer, while his partner has no natural inclination; rather nature prevents. So the inference from the complete to the deficient in a ruling averted by suspicions is invalid. And giving preponderance by prohibition is false, because mere prohibition without these meanings is not considered for imposing the hadd. Do you not see that drinking urine does not necessitate the hadd despite complete prohibition.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents a second dispute within the Hanafi school: whether the hadd punishment for zina (adultery) applies to liwat (sodomy) by analogy. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the effective cause (ma'na) of zina—sexual gratification through ejaculation in a prohibited orifice—exists in liwat even more intensely due to higher prohibition and greater waste of sperm. They rely on textual indication (dalalat al-nass). The response, likely from Abu Hanifa's perspective, counters that the complete form of illicit intercourse is zina because it destroys progeny; liwat is deficient because it only wastes sperm without procreation, lacks mutual desire, and can be prevented by withdrawal. Therefore, analogy from the complete to the deficient is invalid, especially in hudud which are averted by suspicions. The argument that mere prohibition suffices is rejected, as not all prohibited acts (like drinking urine) incur hadd. This illustrates the Hanafi usul principle that completeness is the basis and that hudud require strict analogy.

Key Terms
اللواطة (al-liwata): Sodomy.
حد الزنا (hadd al-zina): The prescribed punishment for unlawful sexual intercourse (stoning or flogging).
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): Textual indication; a method of legal interpretation where the meaning is derived from the text's implication rather than explicit wording.
معنى (ma'na): Meaning or effective cause (often synonymous with 'illa in qiyas).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Abu Hanifa reject applying hadd al-zina to liwat?
A) Because liwat is less prohibited than zina.
B) Because liwat is deficient in the effective cause: it does not destroy progeny and lacks mutual desire.
C) Because the text explicitly excludes liwat.
D) Because the hadd is only for vaginal intercourse.

Key Takeaway
In hudud, analogy from a complete cause to a deficient cause is invalid; the complete form must be the basis for the ruling.

The Condition of the Cause for Kaffarah: Refuting Qiyas
Refuting Shafi'i's qiyas for kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the validity of qiyas in establishing kaffarah for intentional killing by identifying the condition of the cause (ambivalent vs. pure) and applying the Hanafi critique.

Core Idea
Kaffarah requires a cause ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility; pure prohibition cannot ground it.

This passage presents a critical usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the extension of kaffarah (expiation) from accidental killing to intentional killing via qiyas. Imam al-Shafi'i argued that if kaffarah is required for accidental killing despite the excuse of mistake, it should be even more required for intentional killing where there is no excuse. The Hanafi author refutes this by examining the nature of the cause, demonstrating that kaffarah requires a cause that is ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility, not purely prohibited.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Qiyas
Read the first part of the passage where the Shafi'i position is stated. Identify the analogy: from accidental killing (khatā) to intentional killing (amd) and from a binding oath that becomes false to a false oath from the start (ghamūs). Recognize the a fortiori (qiyas awla) structure.
Shafi'i argues that if kaffarah is required when there is an excuse, it is more required when there is no excuse.
2
Isolate the Hanafi Objection
Locate the phrase 'this deduction is mistaken' and the subsequent reasoning. The Hanafi objection is that kaffarah is a hybrid of worship and punishment, so its cause must be ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility. Intentional killing is purely prohibited, making it unsuitable as a cause.
The key term is 'dā'ir bayna al-ḥaẓr wa al-ibāḥah' (ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility).
3
Trace the Rationale for the Rule
Understand why ambivalence is necessary: kaffarah has both an element of worship (requires proximity to Allah) and punishment (atonement). A purely prohibited act cannot be a cause because it lacks the ambivalence that makes the act both sinful and potentially expiable through worship.
Compare with pure permissibility (mubāḥ maḥḍ) also not suitable; the cause must be in the middle.
4
Apply the Principle to Other Cases
Notice the examples after the main argument: killing with a large stone (shibh al-amd) does require kaffarah due to semblance of mistake, while killing a harbi musta'min intentionally does not, because the semblance (shubha) lies in the locus, not the act. This shows the principle being applied consistently.
The principle is not just about the act but also about the locus of the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ: أَنَّ الشَّافِعِيَّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ قَالَ: وَجَبَتِ الْكَفَّارَةُ بِالنَّصِّ فِي الْخَطَأِ مِنَ الْقَتْلِ مَعَ قِيَامِ الْعُذْرِ، وَهُوَ الْخَطَأُ، فَكَانَ دَلَالَةً عَلَى وُجُوبِهَا بِالْعَمْدِ; لِعَدَمِ الْعُذْرِ; لِأَنَّ الْخَطَأَ عُذْرٌ مُسْقِطٌ حُقُوقَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى. وَكَذَلِكَ وَجَبَتِ الْكَفَّارَةُ فِي الْيَمِينِ الْمَعْقُودَةِ إِذَا صَارَتْ كَاذِبَةً، فَلَأَنْ تَجِبَ فِي الْغَمُوسِ وَهِيَ كَاذِبَةٌ مِنَ الْأَصْلِ أَوْلَى، فَصَارَتْ دَلَالَةً عَلَيْهِ; لِقِيَامِ مَعْنَى النَّصِّ وَزِيَادَةٍ. لَكِنَّا نَقُولُ: هَذَا الِاسْتِدْلَالُ غَلَطٌ; لِأَنَّ الْكَفَّارَةَ عِبَادَةٌ فِيهَا شَبَهَ بِالْعُقُوبَاتِ لَا تَخْلُو الْكَفَّارَةُ عَنْ مَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ وَالْعُقُوبَةِ، فَلَا تَجِبُ إِلَّا بِسَبَبٍ دَائِرٍ بَيْنَ الْحَظْرِ وَالْإِبَاحَةِ، وَالْقَتْلُ الْعَمْدُ كَبِيرَةٌ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الزِّنَا وَالسَّرِقَةِ، فَلَمْ يَصْلُحْ سَبَبًا، كَالْمُبَاحِ الْمَحْضِ لَا يَصْلُحُ سَبَبًا مَعَ رُجْحَانِ مَعْنَى الْعِبَادَةِ فِي الْكَفَّارَةِ، وَكَذَلِكَ الْكَذِبُ حَرَامٌ مَحْضٌ، وَأَمَّا الْخَطَأُ فَدَائِرٌ بَيْنَ الْوَصْفَيْنِ، وَالْيَمِينُ عَقْدٌ مَشْرُوعٌ، وَالْكَذِبُ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعٍ. وَلَا يَلْزَمُ إِذَا قَتَلَ بِالْحَجَرِ الْعَظِيمِ، فَإِنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْكَفَّارَةَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ ذَكَرَهُ الطَّحَاوِيُّ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ، لِأَنَّ فِيهِ شُبْهَةَ الْخَطَأِ، يُحْتَاطُ فِيهَا، فَتَثْبُتُ بِشُبْهَةِ السَّبَبِ، كَمَا تَثْبُتُ بِحَقِيقَتِهِ، وَذَكَرَهُ الْجَصَّاصُ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ فِي «أَحْكَامِ الْقُرْآنِ». وَقَدْ جَعَلَهُ فِي الْكِتَابِ: شِبْهَ الْعَمْدِ فِي إِيجَابِ الدِّيَةِ عَلَى الْعَاقِلَةِ، فَكَانَ نَصًّا عَلَى الْكَفَّارَةِ. وَإِذَا قَتَلَ مُسْلِمٌ حَرْبِيًّا مُسْتَأْمَنًا عَمْدًا: لَمْ تَلْزَمْهُ الْكَفَّارَةُ مَعَ قِيَامِ الشُّبْهَةِ; لِأَنَّ الشُّبْهَةَ فِي مَحَلِّ الْفِعْلِ فَاعْتُبِرَتْ فِي الْقَوَدِ; لِأَنَّهُ مُقَابَلٌ بِالْمَحَلِّ مِنْ وَجْهٍ، حَتَّى نَافَى الدِّيَةَ.
And from that is that al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The expiation was obligated by the text in the case of accidental killing while the excuse exists, which is the mistake, so it indicated its obligation in intentional killing due to the absence of the excuse, because the mistake is an excuse that drops the rights of Allah Almighty. And likewise, expiation became obligatory in the binding oath when it becomes false, so it should more so be obligatory in the ghammous oath, which is false from the start, so it became an indication of it due to the presence of the meaning of the text and more. But we say: This deduction is mistaken, because expiation is an act of worship that has a resemblance to punishments; expiation is not free from the meaning of worship and punishment, so it is not obligatory except by a cause that is ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility. And intentional killing is a major sin akin to adultery and theft, so it is not suitable as a cause, just as pure permissibility is not suitable as a cause due to the preponderance of the meaning of worship in expiation. And likewise, lying is pure prohibition, while mistake is ambivalent between the two descriptions, and the oath is a legitimate contract, but lying is not legitimate. And it does not follow that if he kills with a large stone, then it obligates expiation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, as mentioned by al-Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, because there is a semblance of mistake in it; caution is exercised regarding it, so it is established by the semblance of the cause, just as it is established by its reality. And al-Jassas, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned it in 'Ahkam al-Quran'. And he made it in the book: quasi-intentional in obligating blood money on the 'aqila, so it was a text on expiation. And if a Muslim kills a warring or protected person intentionally, expiation is not incumbent upon him despite the existence of the semblance, because the semblance is in the locus of the act, so it is considered in qisas because it is opposed to the locus in one way, so that it negates blood money.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the validity of qiyas in establishing expiation (kaffarah). Imam al-Shafi'i argued that if accidental killing requires kaffarah despite the excuse of mistake, then intentional killing (with no excuse) should require it a fortiori (qiyas awla). He also analogized from a false oath that becomes false (yamin ma'qudah) to an inherently false oath (yamin ghamus). The Hanafi author refutes this, stating that the kaffarah is a hybrid of worship (ibadah) and punishment (uqubah), and therefore requires a cause that is 'ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility' (da'ir bayna al-hazr wa al-ibahah). Intentional killing is purely prohibited (like zina and theft), so it cannot be the cause. Similarly, lying in a ghamus oath is purely prohibited, while accidental killing and the binding oath have an element of ambiguity. The author then explains that certain cases like killing with a large stone (which is quasi-intentional, shibh al-amd) do require kaffarah under Abu Hanifa because of a semblance of mistake, and the killing of a harbi musta'min does not because the semblance lies in the locus (the person is not protected).

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffārah): Expiation; a religious penalty for certain sins, such as killing or breaking an oath.
خطأ (khaṭa): Mistake; error; unintentional act.
عمد (ʿamd): Intentional; deliberate act.
غموس (ghamūs): A false oath taken deliberately from the outset, knowing it is false.
دائر بين الحظر والإباحة (dā'ir bayna al-ḥaẓr wa al-ibāḥah): Ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility; a cause that has both aspects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, what is the key condition for making qiyas to establish expiation (kaffarah)?
A) The cause must be purely prohibited.
B) The cause must be purely permissible.
C) The cause must be ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility.
D) The cause must involve an oath.

Key Takeaway
For expiation (kaffarah), the cause must be ambivalent between prohibition and permissibility; thus, intentional killing (pure prohibition) cannot be analogized from accidental killing.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Refuting the Analogy for Kaffarah in Intentional Murder
Refutes a flawed analogy between intentional murder and false oaths regarding kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects the analogy that kaffarah is obligatory for intentional murder, and identify the key condition (dā'ir bayn al-ḥaẓr wa al-ibāḥah) that governs the obligation of kaffarah.

Core Idea
Kaffarah requires a cause that is mixed between prohibition and permission; intentional murder is purely prohibited, so no kaffarah.

In this passage, al-Bazdawi engages in a critical refinement of an opposing argument that seeks to extend the obligation of kaffarah from accidental killing and false oaths to intentional murder. He exposes a fundamental flaw in the opposing analogy: kaffarah is not a pure punishment but a worship that resembles punishment, and therefore its cause cannot be purely prohibited or purely permissible. By understanding this condition, we see the precision of Hanafi usul in defining the scope of obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opposing Analogy
Read the first two sentences of the passage. The opponent argues: since kaffarah is required for accidental killing (with an excuse) and for a broken bound oath, then it should be even more required for intentional murder (a greater sin without excuse). Identify the qiyas structure: asl (accidental killing / false oath), far' (intentional murder), and the apparent illa (greater sin).
The opponent uses a 'from greater to lesser' reasoning (qiyas al-awlawi), which is a type of qiyas.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Refutation
The Hanafi response begins: 'But we say: This inference is mistaken.' Focus on the claim that kaffarah is a worship with a penal aspect and that it requires a cause that is 'dā'ir bayn al-ḥaẓr wa al-ibāḥah' (between prohibition and permission). Understand that intentional murder is purely prohibited (haram mahd), so it cannot serve as a cause.
The condition that the cause must have an element of permissibility or at least not be purely prohibited is central to Hanafi theory of kaffarah.
3
Trace the Exception Cases
The text then discusses two exceptions: killing with a large stone (shubhat al-khaṭa') and killing a musta'min. For the stone, kaffarah is required due to a semblance of accident; for the musta'min, kaffarah is not required despite the semblance because the semblance is in the locus (the victim's status), not in the act. Note how the Hanafis apply the same principle consistently.
These exceptions demonstrate the nuanced application of the condition: the cause must be mixed in a specific way.
4
Connect to the Quranic Evidence
The passage cites Quran 5:45: 'al-nafs bil-nafs' (the soul for the soul). Explain how this verse establishes qisas for intentional killing but does not mention kaffarah, thereby indicating that kaffarah is not required for pure intentional killing. This is not an explicit prohibition but an inference from silence (mafhūm al-mukhālafah).
The verse's dalālah is considered zannī, but it supports the Hanafi position.
5
Extract the Usul Principle
In the concluding part, the text compares the kaffarah issue with sajdah al-sahw (forgetfulness prostration) and with the kaffarah for breaking fast by intercourse. In all cases, the Hanafis apply the principle that an act with a mixed nature (between worship and punishment) requires a cause with similar mixed nature. Understand how this principle governs the derivation of rulings through istidlāl (inference based on meaning) rather than mere qiyās.
This illustrates the Hanafi methodology of ta'līl and the rejection of qiyās when the condition is not met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخطأ من القتل مع قيام العذر، وهو الخطأ، فكان دلالة على وجوبها بالعمد ؛ لعدم العذر ؛ لأن الخطأ عذر مسقط حقوق الله تعالى.
وكذلك وجبت الكفارة فى اليمين المعقودة إذا صارت كاذبةً، فلأن تجب في الغموس وهي كاذبة من الأصل أولى، فصارت دلالةً عليه ؛ لقيام معنى النص وزيادة.
لكنا نقول: هذا الاستدلال غلط؛ لأن الكفارة عبادةٌ فيها شبهة بالعقوبات لا تخلو الكفارة عن معنى العبادة والعقوبة، فلا تجب إلا بسبب دائر بين الحظر والإباحة، والقتل العمد كبيرة بمنزلة الزنا والسرقة، فلم يصلح سبباً، كالمباح المحض لا يصلح سبباً مع رجحان معنى العبادة في الكفارة، وكذلك الكذبُ حرام محض، وأما الخطأ فدائر بين الوصفين، واليمين عقد مشروع، والكذب غير مشروع.
ولا يلزم إذا قتل بالحَجَر العظيم، فإنه يوجب الكفارة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وذكرها الطحاوي رحمه الله، لأن فيه شُبهة الخطأ، يُحتاط فيها، فتثبت بشبهة السبب، كما تثبت بحقيقته، وذكره الجصاص رحمه الله في أحكام القرآن». وقد جعله في الكتاب : شبه العمد في إيجاب الدية على العاقلة، فكان نصاً على الكفارة.
وإذا قتل مسلم حربياً مستأمناً عمداً: لم تلزمه الكفارة مع قيام الشبهة؛ لأن الشبهة في محل الفعل فاعتُبرت في القود؛ لأنه مقابل بالمحل من وجه، حتى نافى الدية.
وفيه إشارة النص، وهو قوله تعالى : النَّفْسَ بِالنَّفْسِ ) المائدة / ٤٥، فأما الفعل فعمد محض خالص لا تردُّدَ فيه، والكفارة جزاء للفعل المحض.
وفي مسألة الحَجَر : الشبهة في نفس الفعل، فعمت القود والكفارة. ولهذا قلنا: إن سجود السهو لا يجب بالعمد، ولا يصلح أن يكون السهو دليلاً على العمد ؛ لما قلنا، خلافاً للشافعي أيضاً.
وقلنا نحن إن كفارة الفطر وجبت على الرجل بالمواقعة نصاً، ومعنى الفطر فيه معقول لغةً، فوجبت به الكفارة على المرأة أيضاً، استدلالاً به.
Accidental killing, with the excuse of error, indicates the obligation of kaffarah for intentional killing because there is no excuse; for error is an excuse that drops the rights of Allah. Similarly, kaffarah became obligatory in a bound oath when it becomes false, so that it should be obligatory in the false oath (al-ghamus) which is false from the outset, even more so. Thus it becomes an indication by the existence of the textual meaning and more. But we say: This inference is mistaken, because kaffarah is an act of worship with an element of punishment; it is not free from the meaning of worship and punishment, so it is only obligatory due to a cause that is between prohibition and permission. Intentional murder is a major sin like adultery and theft, so it is not a suitable cause, just as pure permission is not a suitable cause when the meaning of worship outweighs in kaffarah. Likewise, lying is pure prohibition. As for error, it is between the two descriptions; and the oath is a legitimate contract, while lying is not legitimate. And it does not follow that if one kills with a large stone, it obligates kaffarah according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, as mentioned by al-Tahawi, may Allah have mercy on him, because there is a semblance of error in it, out of caution, so it is established by a semblance of the cause, just as it is established by its reality. And al-Jassas mentioned it in Ahkam al-Qur'an. And he made it in the book: quasi-intentional in obligating blood money on the 'aqilah, so it was a text for kaffarah. And if a Muslim intentionally kills a harbi (enemy combatant) who is a musta'min (one given aman), kaffarah is not obligatory upon him despite the semblance, because the semblance is in the locus of the act, so it is considered for qisas because it is related to the locus in some way, such that it negates blood money. And there is an indication of the text: His saying, the Exalted: 'the soul for the soul' (al-Ma'idah 5:45). As for the act, it is purely intentional with no hesitation, and kaffarah is a recompense for the pure act. In the stone case, the semblance is in the act itself, so it covers both qisas and kaffarah. For this reason we said: The prostration of forgetfulness is not obligatory due to intention, and forgetfulness is not a proof for intention, due to what we said, contrary to al-Shafi'i as well. And we said: The kaffarah of breaking the fast is obligatory upon the man by intercourse by text, and the meaning of breaking the fast is understood linguistically, so kaffarah became obligatory upon the woman by analogy, by way of deduction (istidlal).
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul dispute) between the Hanafi school and an unnamed opponent (possibly al-Shafi'i or others) regarding the derivation of kaffarah (expiation) for intentional murder. The opponent argues by analogy with accidental killing and false oaths: since kaffarah is obligatory for accidental killing and for a broken oath, it should be even more obligatory for intentional murder (a major sin). The Hanafis refute this analogy on the basis of the nature of kaffarah: it is a worship that resembles a punishment, so it requires a cause that is neither purely prohibited nor purely permissible. Intentional murder is purely prohibited, like adultery and theft, so it cannot be a cause for kaffarah. Accidental killing has an element of error which is an excuse, so it falls between prohibition and permission. Similarly, a false oath in a bound oath (yanim mun'aqidah) has an element of legitimacy (the oath is a contract), while a false oath (al-ghamus) is purely prohibited. The text then discusses exceptions: killing with a large stone (which resembles accident) obligates kaffarah according to Abu Hanifa due to a semblance of error. Also, killing a musta'min (protected non-Muslim) intentionally does not require kaffarah because the semblance is in the locus (the victim's status) and not in the act itself. The text cites the Quranic verse 'al-nafs bil-nafs' as support. The comparison with prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) is used to clarify that forgetfulness (an excuse) cannot be analogized to intention. The passage ends with another example: kaffarah for breaking the fast by intercourse is obligatory on both husband and wife, deduced from the text about the man, because the meaning of breaking the fast is linguistically applicable to both. This showcases Hanafi use of istidlal (deduction) based on meaning.

Key Terms
كفارة (kaffarah): An expiatory act of worship that combines worship and punishment, becoming obligatory due to a cause that is between prohibition and permission.
استدلال (istidlal): An inference based on the meaning of a text and its underlying rationale, as opposed to qiyas (analogy) with a common illah.
دائر بين الحظر والإباحة (dā'ir bayn al-ḥaẓr wa al-ibāḥah): Rotating/mixed between prohibition and permission; a cause that has elements of both, not purely one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is kaffarah not obligatory for intentional murder?
A) Because kaffarah is only for sins committed by mistake
B) Because the cause must be between prohibition and permission, and intentional murder is purely prohibited
C) Because the Quran explicitly exempts intentional murder from kaffarah
D) Because kaffarah is only for oaths

Key Takeaway
Kaffarah is a hybrid act that requires a hybrid cause; intentional murder, being purely prohibited, does not qualify.

The Semblance of Obligation in Suspended Divorce
Establishing that suspended divorce has a semblance of obligation like an oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul rule regarding the semblance of obligation in suspended divorce by tracing the qiyas jaliy from the oath to the suspended divorce.

Core Idea
Suspended divorce has a legal semblance of obligation, requiring a valid locus (marriage) just as an oath requires a garantor.

This passage introduces a key usul principle: the validity of suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) hinges on establishing a connection between the divorce and its locus (marriage). Our Hanafi scholars argue that suspended divorce carries a semblance of obligation (shubhat al-wujub) because it functions like an oath (yamin) that guarantees a dutiful act. To grasp this, we must parse the qiyas jaliy that the author presents, understanding how the analogy between oaths and suspending divorce justifies the need for a locus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
The author states that for a suspended divorce to be valid, there must be a connection (ittisal) between the suspended act and its locus (the marriage). Determine what this claim is and why it matters.
The locus is the marriage that the divorce would dissolve.
2
Trace the qiyas argument
The author compares suspended divorce to an oath (yamin). In an oath, the dutiful act (birr) is guaranteed, creating an obligation. Identify the asl (oath), the illa (intent to guarantee fulfillment), and the far' (suspended divorce). Verify the qiyas panel provided.
3
Extract the semblance of obligation
From the analogy, the author concludes that suspended divorce has a semblance of obligation. Explain how this semblance is established and why it requires a locus.
The semblance (shubha) is not actual obligation but a legal resemblance that triggers certain requirements.
4
Handle the counterargument
The author addresses a case where the suspension is upon marriage (a cause of divorce ownership). Explain how this counterargument is resolved and why the semblance falls away.
This counterargument shows that the rule has exceptions based on the nature of the condition.
5
Apply the rule to ta'liq al-itaq
The author notes that the same principle applies to suspended emancipation (itaq). Confirm the cross-application and why it is consistent.
Consistency in the school's methodology.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطريق أصحابنا لا يصح إلا أن يثبت للمعلق ضَرْبُ اتصال بمحله؛ ليُشترط قيام محله. وأما قيام هذا الملك : فلم يتعين؛ لما بينا أنه ليس بتصرف في الطلاق ليصح باعتبار الملك، والطريق في ذلك أن تعليق الطلاق له شُبهةٌ : بالإيجاب. وبيانه: أن اليمين تُعقد للبر، ولا بد من كون البر مضموناً؛ ليصير واجب الرعاية، فإذا حلف بالطلاق كان البرَّ هو الأصل، وهو مضمون بالطلاق كالمغصوب يلزمه ردُّه ، ويكون مضموناً بالقيمة، فتثبت شبهة وجوب القيمة، فكذلك ها هنا تثبت شبهةً وجوب الطلاق، وقدر ما يجب: لا يُستغنى عن محله. فأما تعليق الطلاق بالنكاح : فتعليق بما هو عله ملك الطلاق، فيصير قدر ما ادعينا من الشبهة مستحقاً به فتسقط هذه الشبهة بهذه المعارضة ومسألة تعليق الطلاق بالنكاح بعد الثلاث: منصوصةٌ في كتاب الطلاق. وفي «الجامع» أيضاً نص في نظيره، وهو العتاق.
The way of our scholars does not validate [a suspended divorce] unless a kind of connection of the suspended act to its locus is established, so that the existence of its locus is a condition. As for the existence of this [right of] ownership: it is not specified; because we have explained that it is not a disposal in divorce to be valid by virtue of ownership, and the method in that is that suspending divorce has a semblance of [causing] obligation. Its explanation: that the oath is contracted for [fulfilling] a dutiful act, and the dutiful act must be guaranteed [by the oath] to become obligatory to observe. So when one swears by divorce, the dutiful act is the original [purpose], and it is guaranteed by divorce, just as a usurped item necessitates its return and is guaranteed by its value. Thus the semblance of obligation of value is established, so likewise here the semblance of obligation of divorce is established. What is obligatory cannot dispense with its locus. As for suspending divorce upon marriage: it is suspending upon what is the cause of the ownership of divorce, so the amount that we claimed of the semblance becomes due by it, and this semblance falls by this counterargument. And the issue of suspending divorce upon marriage after three [divorces] is textually recorded in the Book of Divorce. And in Al-Jami' there is also a text on its equivalent, which is emancipation.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage establishes a usul rule regarding the nature of suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). The author explains that our Hanafi scholars hold that for a suspended divorce to be valid, there must be a connection between the suspended act (the divorce) and its locus (the marriage). This is because the suspended divorce has a semblance (shubha) of obligation (wujub), analogous to an oath (yamin). In an oath, the dutiful act (birr) is guaranteed by the oath, creating an obligation; similarly, the divorce becomes a guarantee of the act. This semblance necessitates a locus (the marriage) for the obligation. If the suspension is upon an event that is the cause of divorce ownership (like marriage), the semblance is satisfied, and the ruling applies. The author notes that this ruling is textually recorded in the Book of Divorce and in Al-Jami' for the analogous case of emancipation (itq).

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspension of a legal effect (like divorce or emancipation) upon the occurrence of a future condition.
شبهة (shubha): A semblance or resemblance of a legal characteristic (here, obligation) that carries certain legal effects.
يمين (yamin): An oath invoking a solemn promise or imprecation, often involving divorce or manumission.

The Validity of Ijaza Without Knowledge of Its Contents
Ruling on ijaza when the recipient lacks knowledge of its contents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ijaza without knowledge of its contents and apply the qiyas of the judge's letter to evaluate similar cases.

Core Idea
An ijaza is invalid if the recipient lacks knowledge of its contents—knowledge is a condition, as with a judge's letter.

This passage examines a key methodological dispute within the Hanafi school: can a license to transmit (ijaza) be valid if the recipient has not read or known its contents? The ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) with the requirement that a witness to a judge's letter must know its contents. This lesson unpacks the qiyas and the intra-school disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: ijaza without knowledge is void.
The first line of the passage explicitly states 'batalat al-ijaza'.
2
Trace the dalil
Identify the analogy used: the case of a judge's letter to another judge, where knowledge of contents is a condition for valid witnessing.
The passage says 'wa aslu dhalika fi kitab al-qadi...'.
3
Compare with Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf allows ijaza in matters customarily kept secret, using custom (urf) as his basis.
He permits it only if one is secure from addition and omission.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The text prefers Abu Hanifa's view as precautionary because allowing ijaza without knowledge opens the door to negligence and innovation.
The analogy with a child's hearing is given: blessed but not proof.
5
Determine the thamarah
The practical consequence: an ijaza given without the recipient knowing its contents is not a valid proof for transmission.
This affects the authenticity of hadith transmission.

وإذا لم يعلم بما فيه : بطلت الإجازة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله ، وصحت في قياس قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله.
وأصل ذلك : في كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي والرسائل: أن عِلْمَ ما فيها شَرْطُ لصحة الإشهاد عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما، خلافاً لأبي يوسف

وإنما جوز ذلك أبو يوسف رحمه الله فيما كان من باب الإسرار في العادة، حتى لم يُجوز في الصكوك.

And if he does not know what is in it, the ijaza is void according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), and it is valid according to the analogy of the statement of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). The basis of that is in the chapter of the judge's letter to the judge and correspondences: that knowledge of what is in them is a condition for the validity of witnessing according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), contrary to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) only permitted that in matters that are customarily kept secret, to the extent that he did not permit it in official documents. Similarly, al-munawalah (handing over) with ijaza is the same as ijaza alone; it is possible that it is not permitted in this chapter and possible that it is permitted out of necessity, and it is only permitted according to him if one is secure from addition and omission. The more precautionary is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). And it is possible that the statement of Abu Yusuf is also like that, because the Sunnah is the foundation of the religion, its matter is great, its affair is serious, and validating ijaza without knowledge and cognizance leads to lifting of trial, cutting off the door of diligence, and opening the door of negligence and innovation. And that is analogous to the hearing of a child who is not qualified to bear (transmission); that is a matter of seeking blessing, not a path by which proof is established. So too this.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage discusses a ruling on the validity of ijaza (license to transmit) when the recipient does not know its contents. The primary position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that such ijaza is void because knowledge of the contents is a condition for its validity. They analogize this to the case of a judge's letter to another judge, where the witness must know the contents of the letter for the testimony to be valid. Abu Yusuf, however, permits ijaza without knowledge in matters that are customarily kept secret, but not in formal documents. He also permits munawalah (handing over) with ijaza under necessity if there is security from tampering. The author notes that the precautionary view is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but also suggests that Abu Yusuf's view may be similar when considering the importance of the Sunnah. Allowing ijaza without knowledge could lead to laxity and innovation. Finally, the author compares this to the hearing of a child, which is blessed but not a valid proof. Thus, the Hanafi school favors requiring knowledge for ijaza.

Key Terms
إجازة (ijāzah): A license or permission granted by a scholar to another to transmit his hadith or teachings.
علم (ʿilm): Knowledge or cognizance of the contents of the ijaza.

Proof of Qiyas from Quran and Sunnah
Proofs for qiyas from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic and prophetic proofs for the validity of qiyas and explain how the Hanafi school uses them to establish qiyas as a legitimate source of law.

Core Idea
Qiyas is validated by the Quranic command 'i'tibar' and the Prophet's own analogical reasoning in multiple hadith.

This passage presents the proofs from Quran and Sunnah that establish qiyas as a valid method for deriving Islamic rulings. The Hanafi school relies on these proofs to justify analogical reasoning. The author cites the Quranic verse 'fa'tabiru' and several hadith where the Prophet used analogical questions, demonstrating that qiyas is rooted in revelation, not mere human speculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses
Find the two Quranic verses cited (al-Hashr 59:2 and al-Anbiya 21:79) and explain how they support the use of analogy.
The verse 'fa'tabiru' is a direct command to consider and compare, while the verse about Solomon highlights judgment without explicit text.
2
Analyze the hadith of the Khath'amiyyah woman
Examine how the Prophet used the analogy of a debt to show that performing Hajj on behalf of another is valid.
The rhetorical question 'ara'ayta' (do you see?) prompts analogical thinking.
3
Examine the hadith of 'Umar on kissing while fasting
See how the Prophet compared kissing to rinsing the mouth, demonstrating a clear analogy.
This shows that even actions that might seem problematic can be evaluated via qiyas.
4
Evaluate the hadith on reward for lawful desires
Understand the analogy: if unlawful actions incur sin, then lawful actions can earn reward.
This hadith is often cited to prove that intentions matter, but here it serves as a proof for qiyas.
5
Synthesize the overall argument
Combine the Quranic command and prophetic practice to conclude that qiyas is a legitimate source of law.
The multiple hadith show the Prophet himself practiced qiyas, so it cannot be purely speculative.

ووجه القول الآخر: أن الله تبارك وتعالى أمرنا بالاعتبار عاماً بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَأْولِي الْأَبْصَرِ ﴾ الحشر / ۲ ، وهو عليه الصلاة والسلام أحق الناس بهذا الوصف.
وقال الله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿فَفَهَمْنَهَا سُلَيْمَنَ الأنبياء /۷۹ ، وذلك عبارةٌ عن الرأي من غير نص.
وكذلك قوله تبارك وتعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ ظَلَمَكَ بِسُؤَالِ نَعْجَنِكَ إِلَى نِعَاجِهِ . سورة ص / ٢٤ : جواب بالرأي.
وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم للخثعمية رضي الله عنها: «أرأيت لو كان على أبيكِ دَيْنٌ فقضيتيه، أما كان يُقبل منك؟ قالت: نعم، قال: فدين الله أحق» (۱).
(۱) حديث الخَثْعَمية : تقدم في باب بيان صفة حكم الأمر [ص١٣٦]، وله ألفاظ أخر، منها: عن ابن عباس أن امرأة من حَنْعَم قالت: يا رسول الله ! إن أبي أدركته فريضة الله في الحج شيخاً كبيراً لا يستطيع أن يستوي على ظهر بعيره، قال: فحجي عنه». رواه الجماعة.
وأخرجه الشافعي عن سليمان بن يسار عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، وفيه: «فقالت: یا رسول الله ! فهل ينفعه ذلك؟ فقال: نعم، كما لو كان عليه دين فقضيتيه : نَفَعَه ، وهذا أقرب لمقصود المصنّف.
وأصرح منه ما رواه البخاري عن ابن عباس أن امرأةً من جهينة جاءت إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : إن أمي نذرت أن تحج، فلم تحج حتى ماتت، أفأحج عنها ؟ قال : نعم، حجي عنها ، أرأيت لو كان على أمك دين أكنت قاضيته؟
وقال لعمر رضي الله عنه وقد سأله عن القبلة للصائم: «أرأيت تمضمضت بماء، ثم مَجَجْتَه أكان يَضرك؟»، وهذا قياس ظاهر. وقال فيمن أتى أهله إنه يُؤجَر، فقيل أيُؤجر أحدنا في شهوته؟! : فقال : «أرأيت لو وضعه في حرام أما كان يأثم؟» .
وقال في حرمة الصدقة على بني هاشم: «أرأيت لو تمضمضت بماء، قالت نعم قال : فاقضوا الله فهو أحق بالوفاء»، وأخرجه النسائي بمعناه.
حديث عمر : أبو داود والنسائي وأحمد وابن حبان عن عمر بن الخطاب قال: «هَشَشتُ، فقبَّلت وأنا صائم، فجئتُ إلى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقلت: صنعتُ اليوم أمراً عظيماً ، قال : وما هو ؟ قال : قلت قبلتُ وأنا صائم، قال: أرأيت لو تمضمضت من الماء؟ قال : إذاً لا يضر ، فقال : ففيم؟». وفي لفظ : أرأيت لو تمضمضت من الماء وأنت صائم؟ قلت: لا بأس به، قال:
حديث أيُؤجر أحدنا في شهوته مسلم عن أبي ذر قال: «قالوا: يا رسول الله ! ذهب أهل الدثور بالأجور يصلون كما نصلي ويصومون كما نصوم، ويتصدقون بفضل أموالهم قال : أو ليس قد جعل الله لكم ما تصدقون به، إن بكل تسبيحة صدقة، وكل تكبيرة صدقة، وكل تحميدة صدقة وكل تهليلة صدقة، وأمر بالمعروف صدقة، ونهي عن منكر صدقة ، وفي بضع أحدكم صدقة.
قالوا: يا رسول الله أيأتي أحدنا شهوته ويكون له فيها أجر؟ قال: أرأيتم لو وضعها في حرام أكان عليه فيها وزر؟ قالوا: نعم ، قال : كذلك إذا وضعها في الحلال: كان له أجر
وأخرجه الترمذي، وزاد فيه : تبسمك في وجه أخيك صدقةٌ، وإرشادك الرجل الطريق صدقةٌ، وإماطتك الحَجَرَ والشوك والعَظمَ عن الطريق، وإفراغك من دلوك في دلو أخيك صدقة».
And the argument of the other opinion: that Allah, blessed and exalted, commanded us to consider (i'tibar) generally by His saying: 'So take example, O people of insight' (Surah al-Hashr 59:2), and he (peace and blessings be upon him) is the most entitled of people to this description. And Allah, blessed and exalted, said: 'And We gave understanding of it to Solomon' (Surah al-Anbiya 21:79), and that is an expression of opinion without text. And likewise His saying, blessed and exalted: 'He has certainly wronged you in demanding your ewe in addition to his ewes' (Surah Sad 38:24): a response by opinion. And the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said to the Khath'amiyyah woman (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Do you see that if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be accepted from you?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'So the debt of Allah is more deserving.' And he said to 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when he asked about kissing while fasting: 'Do you see that if you rinsed your mouth with water and then spat it out, would it harm you?' This is an apparent analogy. And he said regarding one who goes to his wife that he is rewarded. It was said: 'Are we rewarded for our desires?' He said: 'Do you see that if he placed it in something forbidden, would he not be sinning?' And he said regarding the prohibition of charity upon Banu Hashim: 'Do you see that if you rinsed your mouth with water...' she said: 'Yes.' He said: 'So fulfill (the obligations of) Allah, for He is more deserving of fulfillment.'
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a source of Islamic law, responding to those who reject it. The author presents the 'other opinion' (al-qawl al-akhar) which holds that qiyas is legitimate. The first proof is the Quranic command 'fa'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (take example, O people of insight). The word i'tibar implies drawing conclusions through analogy. The Prophet is the most entitled to act on this command. Second, the verse about Prophet Solomon (understanding without explicit text) and Prophet David's judgment (by opinion) show that using one's reasoning is sanctioned. Third, numerous hadith demonstrate the Prophet himself used analogical reasoning: the hadith of the Khath'amiyyah woman comparing the debt owed to Allah to a human debt; the hadith of 'Umar comparing kissing while fasting to rinsing the mouth; the hadith about reward for lawful desires compared to sin for unlawful ones; and the hadith about charity for Banu Hashim compared to rinsing. Each hadith begins with 'ara'ayta' (do you see?), which is a rhetorical device prompting analogical thinking. The text thus establishes qiyas as a valid method derived from revelation.

Key Terms
اعتبار (i'tibar): The act of considering or drawing analogies, used by the author as a basis for qiyas.
رأي (ra'y): Personal opinion or reasoning, often used in the context of ijtihad and qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) That women are allowed to perform Hajj on behalf of others
D) That charity is not allowed for Banu Hashim

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid source of Islamic law because it is commanded by the Quran and practiced by the Prophet himself.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Prophetic Practice as Proof of Qiyas
Proof of qiyas from Prophetic practice and infallible ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Prophet's use of analogical reasoning in the cited hadiths demonstrates the validity of qiyas as a source of law, and explain the Hanafi argument that the Prophet's ijtihad is infallible.

Core Idea
The Prophet himself used qiyas; his ijtihad is infallible, establishing qiyas as a binding proof.

This passage presents three key examples from the Prophet's own practice where he employed analogical reasoning to derive rulings. By analyzing these hadiths, we see that qiyas is not a human innovation but a method blessed by divine guidance. The passage further argues that the Prophet's complete knowledge makes his ijtihad infallible, thus his use of qiyas is authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Prophetic analogies
Read the three hadith examples: the kissing while fasting analogy, the reward for lawful desire analogy, and the impurity analogy for Banu Hashim. Note the structure: the Prophet compares a new case to a known ruling.
Each hadith uses the phrase 'ar'ayta' (do you not see) to introduce the analogy.
2
Classify the evidence
These hadiths are ahad reports (zanni al-thubut) but their indicative meaning (dalala) is clear. They show the Prophet actively performing qiyas.
The Hanafi school accepts ahad hadith as proof in usul.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
Prophetic actions (fi'l al-rasul) are a source of law. When the Prophet uses qiyas, it establishes that qiyas is a valid method of istinbat.
The principle: 'The Prophet's practice is evidence; his use of a method validates that method.'
4
Analyze the infallibility argument
The passage argues that the Prophet had complete knowledge of texts (mutashabih/mujmal), so his ijtihad is free from error and divine confirmation (from Allah) makes his rulings decisive.
This distinguishes Prophetic ijtihad from that of other mujtahids, who may err.
5
Derive the ruling
Since the Prophet's use of qiyas is correct and confirmed, qiyas is a valid source of law for the community.
The practical effect: mujtahids may use qiyas when no explicit text exists.

وقال لعمر رضي الله عنه وقد سأله عن القبلة للصائم: «أرأيت تمضمضت بماء، ثم مَجَجْتَه أكان يَضرك؟»، وهذا قياس ظاهر. وقال فيمن أتى أهله إنه يُؤجَر، فقيل أيُؤجر أحدنا في شهوته؟! : فقال : أرأيت لو وضعه في حرام أما كان يأثم؟» . وقال في حرمة الصدقة على بني هاشم: «أرأيت لو تمضمضت بماء، ثم مججته أكنت شاربه؟!». وهذا قياس واضح في تحريم الأوساخ بحكم الاستعمال. ولأن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم أسبق الناس في العلم، حتى وَضَحَ له ما خفي على غيره من المتشابه والمجمل، فمن المحال أن يخفى عليه معاني النص، وإذا وَضَحَ له : لزمه العمل به ؛ لأن الحجة : للعمل شرعت، إلا أن اجتهاد غيره يحتمل الخطأ، واجتهاده لا يحتمل، ولا يحتمل القرار على الخطأ، فإذا أقره الله تعالى على ذلك: دلّ على أنه مصيب بيقين. وذلك مثلُ أمور الحرب، وقد كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يشاوِر في سائر الحوادث عند عدم النص مثل مشاورته في أمور
And he said regarding 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he asked about kissing for the fasting person: 'Do you not see that if you rinsed your mouth with water, then spat it out, would it harm you?' This is an apparent analogy. And he said regarding one who came to his wife (in Ramadan) that he is rewarded; it was said, 'Is any of us rewarded for his desire?' So he said: 'Do you not see that if he had placed it in the unlawful, would he not be sinful?' And he said regarding the prohibition of charity upon Banu Hashim: 'Do you not see that if you rinsed your mouth with water, then spat it out, would you drink it?' This is a clear analogy regarding the prohibition of impurities due to use. And because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was the foremost of people in knowledge, until that which was ambiguous and general became clear to him that was hidden from others, so it is impossible that the meanings of the text were hidden from him. And when it became clear to him, he was obliged to act upon it, because the proof was legislated for action. However, the ijtihad of others is susceptible to error, while his ijtihad is not susceptible, and he is not susceptible to persisting in error. So when Allah, the Exalted, confirmed him upon that, it indicates that he is correct with certainty. That is like matters of war, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to consult in various incidents when there was no text, like his consultation in matters.
Source pages p. 517

Commentary
This passage presents two hadith examples demonstrating the Prophet's use of analogical reasoning (qiyas) to derive rulings. The first is the famous hadith of 'Umar asking about kissing while fasting; the Prophet uses an analogy with rinsing the mouth, which does not break the fast. The second is about being rewarded for lawful marital relations, using an analogy with sin in unlawful relations. The third example analogizes impurity from use. The commentator then argues that the Prophet's ijtihad is infallible due to his complete knowledge, and his rulings are decisive. Since Allah confirmed him, his analogies are correct. The passage thus establishes qiyas as a valid proof in Islamic law, rooted in the practice of the Prophet himself.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning, as used by the Prophet himself in the examples given to derive legal rulings.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent reasoning by a qualified jurist to derive rulings from sources.
المتشابه والمجمل (al-mutashabih wa al-mujmal): Ambiguous and general texts whose meanings are unclear to others but were clear to the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of citing the hadith about 'Umar asking about kissing while fasting in this passage?
A) To prove that kissing breaks the fast.
B) To demonstrate that qiyas is a valid method of legal reasoning.
C) To show the Prophet's leniency in fasting.
D) To prove that rinsing the mouth invalidates the fast.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's own use of analogical reasoning in the cited hadiths, combined with the argument of his infallible ijtihad, establishes qiyas as a legitimate and authoritative method for deriving rulings in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Obligation of Taqlid in Matters Beyond Qiyas
Usul rule with examples and internal disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between matters accessible and inaccessible to qiyas, and apply the Hanafi rule that taqlid is obligatory in the latter while ra'y is permitted in the former.

Core Idea
In matters reason cannot reach, only transmitted authority binds us; in rational matters, ra'y is permissible.

How do we know rulings that human reason cannot derive on its own? The Hanafi school answers: through transmitted reports (sunnah, athar). This lesson explains the epistemological boundary between matters that can be reached by qiyas and those that require pure taqlid. By studying the examples—from menstruation periods to transactions—you will understand why the school insists on following transmitted authority when reason has no path.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of rulings
Read the passage and note the distinction between 'ma la yudraku bi al-qiyas' (matters not perceived by qiyas) and 'ma yu'qalu bi al-qiyas' (matters intelligible by qiyas). The legal consequence differs: taqlid vs. ra'y.
The categories are defined by whether human reason can independently deduce the ruling.
2
Recognize the examples of non-qiyas matters
The passage gives three examples: menstruation limits (3-10 days), prohibition of 'ina transactions (Aisha's hadith), and (implicitly) the pregnant woman divorce according to some narrations. These rulings are not reachable by analogy; they are based purely on transmitted reports.
The Hanafi school accepts these reports despite their zanni thubut because no qiyas alternative exists.
3
Analyze the internal disagreements
Examine the disputes: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf differ from a transmitted report on pregnant divorce? Actually, the text shows that on the hired worker, Abu Hanifa used ra'y to oppose a report from Ali. Understand that such ikhtilaf is valid only in matters accessible to qiyas; in non-qiyas matters, the school agrees on taqlid.
The internal disputes highlight that when qiyas is possible, ra'y may override a report if the report is weak or contradictory.
4
Understand the epistemological rationale
The author argues that in non-qiyas matters, the only alternative to accepting the report is to deny the prophetic source (تكذيب), which is false. Therefore, acting on the report is obligatory.
This is a strong epistemological claim: rejection of a sound report in these matters amounts to rejecting revelation itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(بياض في الأصل). (۲) قوله : الأجير المشترك ضامِنٌ، ورَوَيَا ذلك عن علي: لم أقف عليه من روايتهم، وإنما رواه ابن أبي شيبة من طرق ليس لهم فيها ذكر، وقد رواه محمد في الأصل» عن عمر رضي الله عنه. ٥٢٦ (1) ذلك عن أنس وعثمان بن أبي العاص الثقفي رضي الله عنهما. وأفسدوا شراء ما باع بأقل مما ،باع، عملاً بقول عائشة (٢) عنها في قصة زيد بن أرقم رضي الله عنه. الله رضي أما فيما لا يُدرك بالقياس : فلا بد من العمل به ؛ حَمْلاً لذلك على التوقيف من رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا وجه له غير هذا إلا التكذيب، وذلك باطل، فوجب العمل به، لا محالة. فأما فيما يُعقل بالقياس: فوجه قول الكرخي رحمه الله : أن القول (۳) ۹ بالرأي من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مشهور ) ، واحتمال الخطأ (۱) قوله : ورووا ذلك عن أنس وعثمان بن أبي العاص : أما قول أنس: فذكره محمد في «الأصل» بلاغاً. وقال الكرخي في «المختصر: ثنا نصر بن القاسم ثنا أبو همام ثنا يحيى عن أنا الثوري ح نصر ثنا همام ثنا مخلد بن الحسين عن ابن عليَّة قالا : حدثنا الجلد بن أيوب عن معاوية بن قُرَّة عن أنس قال: «الحيض ثلاث أربع خمس : ست سبع ثمان تسع عشر، فما زاد : فهي استحاضة». هي وأما قول عثمان : فأخرجه ابن أبي شيبة بلفظ : لا تكون المرأة مستحاضة في يوم ولا يومين حتى تبلغ عشرة ، وهذا ليس حجةً من كل وجه، والله أعلم. (۲) قوله : عملاً بقول عائشة : عن امرأة أبي إسحاق أنها دخلت على عائشة وأم ولد لزيد بن أرقم ، فقالت أم ولد زيد لعائشة : إني بعتُ من زيد غلامًا بثمانمائة نسيئة، واشتريته بستمائة نقدًا، فقالت : أبلغي زيدًا أن قد أبطلت جهادك مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا أن تتوب بئس ما اشتريت، وبئس ما شريت». رواه أحمد، وقال في «التنقيح»: إسناده جيد. درهم (۳) قوله : القول بالرأي من الصحابة مشهورٌ : يَشهد بذلك كتاب ابن أبي شيبة
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said: The pregnant woman is divorced three times for the sunna, and it has been narrated from Jabir and Ibn Mas'ud contrary to that. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The joint hired worker is a guarantor, and they narrated that from Ali, and Abu Hanifa opposed them in that by opinion. And the practice of our companions has agreed upon taqlid in what is not intelligible by qiyas. For they said regarding the minimum of menstruation: it is three days and its maximum: ten days, and they narrated that from Anas and Uthman ibn Abi al-As. And they invalidated selling what one bought for less than what one sold, acting upon the saying of Aisha in the story of Zayd ibn Arqam. As for what is not perceived by qiyas: it is necessary to act upon it; attributing that to the prophetic instruction from the Messenger of God has no other face except denial, and that is false, so acting upon it is obligatory, without exception. As for what is intelligible by qiyas: the opinion of al-Karkhi is that the use of ra'y by the Companions of the Prophet is well-known, and the possibility of error...
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a statement of a fundamental usul principle in the Hanafi school: the distinction between matters that can be understood through rational analogy (qiyas) and those that cannot. The author begins by citing two specific fiqh disputes as examples. First, regarding the divorce of a pregnant woman: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that she can be divorced three times in accordance with the sunna, while a narration from Jabir and Ibn Mas'ud reports that the sunna is to divorce her only once. Second, regarding the joint hired worker (ajir mushtarak): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that he is a guarantor (dammin), citing a report from Ali, while Abu Hanifa opposes this using his own reasoning (ra'y). The author then states that the Hanafi school has agreed on taqlid (following transmitted authority) in matters that are not comprehensible by qiyas. Examples given: the minimum and maximum duration of menstruation (three and ten days, respectively) are based on reports from Anas and Uthman ibn Abi al-As, not on rational deduction. Similarly, the invalidation of a transaction where one sells an item and then buys it back for less (a form of 'ina) is based on the saying of Aisha regarding Zayd ibn Arqam. The author then explains the rationale: in matters not accessible to qiyas, acting on transmitted reports is obligatory because the only alternative would be to deny the prophetic source, which is invalid. In matters that are accessible to qiyas, al-Karkhi's opinion is presented: the use of ra'y by the Companions is well-known, and despite the possibility of error, it is accepted. The passage thus establishes the epistemic weight of transmitted reports when reason cannot independently arrive at the ruling.

Key Terms
ما لا يُدرك بالقياس (ma la yudraku bi al-qiyas): Matters whose rulings cannot be deduced by rational analogy and must be known through textual transmission.
ما يُعقل بالقياس (ma yu'qalu bi al-qiyas): Matters whose rulings can be derived through rational analogy, where the use of ra'y is permissible.
التقليد (al-taqlid): Accepting and following a transmitted report or ruling without demanding a rational proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because such reports are always mutawatir and certain.
B) Because the only alternative is to deny the prophetic source, which is false.
C) Because the Companions unanimously agreed on taqlid.
D) Because qiyas is forbidden in all matters.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, transmitted reports must be followed in matters beyond the reach of rational analogy, while ra'y is permissible where qiyas can operate.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Hanafi Categorization of Companion Statements: Tawqif vs. Ra'y
Classifying Sahabi statements by knowability through qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tawqifi and qiyasi Companion statements and apply the Hanafi rule that only tawqifi statements are binding.

Core Idea
A Companion's statement is binding only in matters unknowable by analogy; in qiyasi matters, follow their method of ijtihad, not their specific ruling.

This passage from the commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul presents a key Hanafi rule: the authority of a Companion's statement depends on whether the matter can be known by qiyas. The commentator explains that in matters of pure revelation (tawqif), the Companion's statement is a binding transmission from the Prophet. But in matters accessible to reason and analogy, the Companions themselves used their own ijtihad and allowed disagreement, so we must follow their method of reasoning, not their individual conclusions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the first two sentences. What are the two kinds of Companion statements based on knowability through qiyas? One is tawqif (not known by qiyas), the other is comprehensible by qiyas.
The text says: 'As for what cannot be known by analogy... As for what can be comprehended by analogy.'
2
State the ruling for tawqifi matters
Explain why acting on the Companion's statement is necessary. The text argues that the only alternative is denial, which is false, so action is obligatory.
The binding nature comes from treating it as revelation (tawqif) from the Prophet.
3
State the ruling for qiyasi matters
Determine why taqlid of a Companion is not allowed. The text cites al-Karkhi: the Companions used ra'y, admitted possibility of error, differed, and did not impose their views. Therefore, we must follow their method (iqtida') not their specific rulings.
Key evidence: Ibn Mas'ud said 'If I err, it is from Satan.'
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
Consider the hadith 'My Companions are like stars.' How does the Hanafi school interpret it? The text says it means following their general example in using ra'y, not blindly following any one Companion.
The footnote discusses the weak chain of this hadith, which limits its probative value.
5
Evaluate the opposing view
Some scholars take the hadith literally to mean following any Companion's specific opinion is guidance. The Hanafi response: the hadith is weak (zanni), and the Companions' own practice contradicts such a literal reading.
This leads to the practical difference: a Hanafi mujtahid may disagree with a Companion's qiyasi ruling, while a literalist would be bound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما فيما لا يُدرك بالقياس : فلا بد من العمل به ؛ حَمْلاً لذلك على التوقيف من رسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا وجه له غير هذا إلا التكذيب، وذلك باطل، فوجب العمل به، لا محالة.
فأما فيما يُعقل بالقياس: فوجه قول الكرخي رحمه الله : أن القول بالرأي من أصحاب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مشهور ، واحتمال الخطأ في اجتهادهم كائن، لا محالة.
فقد كان يخالف بعضهم بعضاً، وكانوا لا يَدعون الناس إلى أقوالهم. وكان ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه يقول : إن أخطأت فمن الشيطان.
وإذا كان كذلك: لم يجز تقليد مثله، بل وجب الاقتداء بهم في العمل بالرأي مثل ما عملوا، وذلك معنى قول النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: أصحابي كالنجوم ، بأيهم اقتديتم اهتديتم.
(۱) قوله : وكان ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه يقول : إن أخطأت فمن الشيطان : رواه أبو داود في قصة مَن تزوج ولم يَفرِض، ولفظه: «عن عبد الله بن عتبة بن مسعود أن عبد الله بن مسعود أُتي في رجل بهذا الخبر ، قال : فاختلفوا إليه شهراً - أو قال : مرات - قال : فإني أقول فيها : إن لها صداقاً كصداق نسائها، لا وَكْس ولا شَطَط، وإن لها الميراث، وعليها العدة، فإن يكن صواباً فمن الله، وإن يكن خطأ فمني ومن الشيطان، والله ورسوله بريئان». الحديث، وقد تقدم له طرق.
(۲) حديث : أصحابي كالنجوم: عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: مثل أصحابي في أمتي مثل النجوم، فبأيهم اقتديتم اهتديتم. رواه الدارقطني وابن عبد البر وقال : إسناده لا تقوم به حجة. وأخرجه ابن عدي من حديث عمر بلفظ : «سألت عما يختلف فيه أصحابي ربي من بعدي فقال : يا محمد إن أصحابك عندي بمنزلة النجوم، بعضها أضوء من بعض، فمن أخذ بشيء مما اختلفوا فيه : فهو عندي على هدي». وفي سنده ضعف. وسئل البزار عنه فقال : لا يصح هذا الكلام عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم.
As for what cannot be known by analogy: it is necessary to act upon it; carrying that upon divine instruction from the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) — there is no basis for this other than denial, and that is false, so acting upon it is obligatory, inevitably. As for what can be comprehended by analogy: the position of al-Karkhi (may Allah have mercy on him) is that expressing opinion (ra'y) from the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is well-known, and the possibility of error in their ijtihad exists, inevitably. Indeed, some of them would disagree with others, and they would not call people to their own statements. And Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) used to say: 'If I err, it is from Satan.' And if this is the case: it is not permissible to imitate (taqlid) someone like him (i.e., a Companion's specific opinion), rather it is necessary to follow them in acting upon opinion (ra'y) as they did. And that is the meaning of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement: 'My Companions are like stars; whichever of them you follow, you will be guided.' (1) Commentary on Ibn Mas'ud's statement: narrated by Abu Dawud in the story of a man who married and did not specify a dower... (2) Hadith 'My Companions are like stars': from Ibn 'Umar... its chain is not a proof...
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the usul text presents a fundamental Hanafi rule regarding the authority of the sayings (aqwal) of the Companions. The commentator distinguishes two categories. First, matters that are not rationally comprehensible through analogy (ma la yudraku bi al-qiyas)—these are purely tawqifi (based on revelation) and must be accepted as binding from a Companion because the only alternative is outright denial of the source, which is invalid. Second, matters that are comprehensible through analogy (ma yu'qalu bi al-qiyas)—here the Companions themselves exercised ra'y (personal reasoning/opinion), as stated by Imam al-Karkhi. Their ijtihad was well-known and admitted the possibility of error. The Companions sometimes differed, and they did not compel others to follow their opinions; Ibn Mas'ud even said, 'If I err, it is from Satan.' Therefore, taqlid (blind imitation) of a single Companion's specific ruling is not permissible. Instead, we must follow their method of using ra'y and ijtihad, not their particular conclusions. The commentator cites the famous hadith 'My Companions are like stars' to support this meaning—guidance comes from following their general path, not any one star exclusively. However, the footnote discusses the weakness of this hadith's chain, noting that scholars like al-Bazzar deemed it unsound. The Hanafi position here is a middle way: Companions' statements in non-qiyasi matters are binding (as they are based on revelation), while in qiyasi matters they are examples of ijtihad to be emulated methodologically, not as binding precedents. This opposes a literalist view that every Companion's opinion is an independent source of law.

Key Terms
قول الصحابي (qawl al-sahabi): The statement or opinion of a Companion of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
تقليد (taqlid): Following the specific opinion of a Companion (or other authority) without evidence or ijtihad.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the method or practice of the Companions in using ra'y/analogy, not their specific rulings.
رأي (ra'y): Personal reasoned opinion, often involving qiyas (analogy) in matters not explicitly covered by revelation.
توقيف (tawqif): Divine instruction or revelation, known only by transmission, not by reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how should a Hanafi jurist treat a Companion's statement on a matter that can be known by analogy (qiyas)?
A) It is binding and must be followed without question.
B) It is not binding; one must follow the method of ra'y that the Companions used, not the specific outcome.
C) It is binding only if the Companion was a prominent one like Abu Bakr or Umar.
D) It is completely irrelevant and can be ignored.

Key Takeaway
In qiyasi matters, follow the Companions' method of ijtihad, not their specific rulings; only tawqifi Companion statements are binding.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Preference for Companions' Practice over Qiyas
Criticism of Shafi'i qiyas and defense of Hanafi reliance on Companions' practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi reasons for prioritizing Companions' practice over qiyas and evaluate the criticism of qiyas al-shabah.

Core Idea
Companions' practice is preferred over qiyas due to possible tawqif and superior judgment.

This passage presents a robust defense of the Hanafi methodology regarding the use of Companions' opinions (aqwal al-sahaba) in deriving rulings. The author cites numerous hadiths extolling the knowledge of the Companions, then explains why their practice is given precedence over analogical reasoning (qiyas). He also critiques Imam al-Shafi'i for resorting to weaker forms of qiyas (qiyas al-shabah). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and evaluative contrast between the two schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim
The author's central claim is that the practice and opinions of the Companions are to be given precedence over qiyas. This is based on the authority of Abu Sa'id al-Hanafi.
The claim is not that qiyas is invalid, but that it is secondary.
2
Examine the evidence for Companions' virtue
Numerous hadiths are cited to establish the profound knowledge and divine guidance of key Companions (Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, etc.). This supports the idea that their statements carry special weight.
These hadiths are from Tirmidhi, Bukhari, Muslim, etc., establishing their reliability.
3
Understand the two reasons for prioritization
Abu Sa'id gives two reasons: (1) the possibility that the Companion heard directly from the Prophet (tawqif), and (2) the superiority of their personal judgment (ijtihad) due to their closeness to revelation.
The first reason is stronger: if tawqif is probable, it is like a sunna.
4
Critique of Shafi'i reliance on qiyas al-shabah
The author criticizes Imam al-Shafi'i for abandoning many aspects of the sunna (i.e., Companions' practice) and resorting to qiyas al-shabah, which lacks a clear illa and cannot establish obligation. This is likened to acting on istishab without evidence.
Qiyas al-shabah: analogy based on resemblance to multiple origins, considered weak in Hanafi usul.
5
Conclude the Hanafi superiority
The passage ends with high praise for the Hanafi school as the ultimate path that combines principles and branches perfectly.
The author asserts that the religion reached perfection through the Hanafi imams.

Uthman, twelve years of caliphate, Ali completed the thirty. Al-Tirmidhi said: hasan, and Ibn Hibban and al-Hakim authenticated it. In another wording: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'The caliphate of prophethood is thirty years, then Allah gives the kingdom, or he said: He gives His kingdom to whom He wills.' The green [sky] has not shaded nor the dry [earth] carried one more truthful than Abu Dharr, he resembles Jesus, peace be upon him, in his piety.' Umar said: Do you recognize that for him, O Messenger of Allah? He said: Yes, so recognize him. Al-Tirmidhi narrated it, and its chain is weak. And from Abdullah ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, embraced me to his chest and said: 'O Allah, make him knowledgeable in religion and teach him interpretation.'
