الله، ولا في سنة رسول الله : فلينظر فيما اجتمع عليه المسلمون، فإن لم يكن فليجتهد رأيه ولا يقل أحدكم إني أخشى، فإن الحلال بين، والحرام بين، وبين ذلك أمور مشتبهة، فدع ما يريبك إلى ما لا يريبك». وأخرج نحوه عن عمر بن الخطاب، دون ما في أوله وآخره، وإسناده صحيح أيضاً، وأخرج البيهقي عن زيد بن ثابت مثله، وإسناده حسن. وقد روينا ما هو قياس بنفسه من النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. وعمل أصحاب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ورضي الله عنهم في هذا الباب ومناظرتهم ومشاورتهم في هذا الباب أشهر من أن تخفى على عاقل مميز. فإن طعن طاعن فيهم : فقد ضل عن سواء السبيل، ونابذ الإسلام. ومن ادعى خصوصهم : فقد ادعى أمراً لا دليل عليه، بل الناس سواء في تكليف الاعتبار. وأما المعقول فهو أن الاعتبار واجب بنص القرآن، وهو النظر والتأمل فيما أصاب من قبلنا من المثلات بأسباب نقلت عنهم؛ احترازاً عن مثله من الجزاء. وكذلك التأملُ في حقائق اللغة ؛ لاستعارة غيرها لها : سائغ، والقياس نظيره بعينه ؛ لأن الشرع شرع أحكاماً بمعان أشار إليها، كما أنزل مثلات بأسباب قصها، ودعانا إلى التأمل، ثم الاعتبار. وبيان ذلك في الأصل في قول الله تعالى: ﴿ هُوَ الَّذِي أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ مِن دِيَرِهِمْ لِأَوَّلِ الْحَشْرِ ﴾ الحشر / ٢ : فالإخراج من الديار عقوبةٌ بمعنى القتل، والكفر يصلح داعياً إليه، وأول الحشر دلالة على تكرار هذه العقوبة.
From Mu'adh ibn Jabal, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, sent him to Yemen and said: 'How will you judge when a matter is presented to you?' He said: 'I will judge by what is in the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If it is not in the Book of Allah?' He said: 'Then by the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If it is not in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'I will exert my own opinion (ijtihad) and will not be remiss.' He said: 'He struck his chest and said: Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases the Messenger of Allah.' Reported by Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi, who said it is 'gharib' and its chain is not continuous in his view, and al-Bukhari said: 'It is not known and not authentic.' And from him (another narration) he said: 'When the Prophet sent me to Yemen, I said: What do you think about what I am asked about when two people come to me with a dispute concerning something not in the Book of Allah and I have not heard it from you?' He said: 'Exert your judgment (ijtihad), for if Allah knows that you are truthful, He will guide you to the truth.' Reported by Sa'id al-Umawi in his book 'al-Maghazi' and al-Khatib in 'al-Faqih wa al-Mutafaqqih'. Ibn Majah has part of it, and in its chain is Muhammad ibn Sa'id al-Maslub, who is ruined (unreliable). But supporting the hadith of Mu'adh is what al-Darimi transmitted with a sound chain from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who said: 'There came a time when we were not asked, and we were not there, then Allah brought us to what you see. So when one of you is asked about something, let him look in the Book of Allah; if he does not find it in the Book of Allah, let him look in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah; if he does not find it in the Book of Allah nor in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, let him look at what the Muslims have agreed upon; if there is none, then let him exert his own opinion and let none of you say 'I fear', for the halal is clear and the haram is clear, and between them are ambiguous matters. So leave what makes you doubt for what does not make you doubt.' And a similar narration was transmitted from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, without its beginning and end, and its chain is also sound. And al-Bayhaqi transmitted from Zayd ibn Thabit a similar report with a good chain. And we have narrated what is qiyas in itself from the Prophet, peace be upon him. And the practice of the Companions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, and may Allah be pleased with them, in this matter, and their debates and consultations in this matter, are more famous than to be hidden from an intelligent person. For if anyone attacks them, he has strayed from the straight path and renounced Islam. And whoever claims that they were special (not to be followed) has claimed something without evidence; rather, all people are equal in the obligation of deriving analogies (i'tibar). As for the rational proof, it is that i'tibar is obligatory by the text of the Quran, namely, reflection and contemplation on what befell those before us of punishments through causes transmitted from them, in order to avoid similar retribution. Similarly, reflection on the realities of language; to use one word metaphorically for another is permissible, and qiyas is its exact equivalent; because the Lawgiver legislated rulings based on meanings to which He pointed, just as He sent down punishments with causes He narrated, and called us to reflect and then derive analogies. The explanation of that in its original form is in the saying of Allah the Exalted: "He it is Who expelled those who disbelieved among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering" (al-Hashr 59:2). For expelling from homes is a punishment in the sense of killing, and disbelief is a suitable cause for it, and 'first gathering' indicates the repetition of this punishment.
Source pages p. 560

Commentary
This passage is from Al-Bazdawi's Usul and serves as a comprehensive proof for qiyas as a source of Islamic law. The author first presents the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, which explicitly shows the Prophet approving of ijtihad (and by extension qiyas) when the Quran and Sunnah provide no direct ruling. Although the hadith has been criticized by some scholars like al-Bukhari and al-Tirmidhi regarding its chain, the author counters by providing supporting narrations from Ibn Mas'ud, 'Umar, and Zayd ibn Thabit that establish the same methodology: Quran, then Sunnah, then Ijma', then ijtihad. This effectively neutralizes the criticism and demonstrates the practice of the Companions. The author then argues that to reject these Companions' practice is to stray from Islam. Next, he presents a rational (aqli) argument: the Quran itself commands i'tibar (reflection on past punishments and their causes) in verses like 'i'tabiru ya uli al-absar' (take lesson, O people of insight). This command implies that we must identify causes ('illal) behind divine acts and apply them to similar situations. Analogous reasoning (qiyas) in law is exactly this: identifying the underlying cause of a ruling and applying it to new cases. The author illustrates with the verse about expelling the People of the Book from their homes: the punishment of expulsion is linked to the cause of disbelief, and the phrase 'first gathering' suggests this punishment can recur when the cause is present. Thus, qiyas is not mere human speculation but a divinely sanctioned method.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in law: applying a known ruling to a new case due to a common effective cause ('illah).
اعتبار (i'tibar): Deriving lessons and analogies from past events or linguistic patterns.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Exerting one's reasoning to derive a ruling when no clear text exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof presented in the passage, what is the Quranic basis for qiyas?
A) The verse 'And obey Allah and obey the Messenger' (al-Nisa 4:59)
B) The command to practice i'tibar (reflection) and the example of Surah al-Hashr 59:2
C) The verse 'This day I have perfected your religion' (al-Ma'idah 5:3)
D) The hadith 'My community will not agree upon an error'

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is established through three proofs: prophetic approval (hadith of Mu'adh), companion practice, and rational reasoning from the Quranic command of i'tibar.

The Quranic and Rational Basis for Qiyas
Proving qiyas from Quran and reason

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic and rational proofs for qiyas and explain how the verse from al-Hashr establishes the obligation of 'ibar.

Core Idea
The Quran commands 'ibar (consideration of causes), making qiyas an obligatory method of legal reasoning.

In this lesson, we examine how al-Bazdawi grounds qiyas in the Quran itself. He argues that the verse in Surah al-Hashr contains a clear cause-effect relationship and a command to reflect, making qiyas not just permissible but obligatory. This rational proof complements the transmitted evidence from the Prophet and Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The author states that 'ibar (consideration) is obligatory by the text of the Quran.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary text is al-Hashr 59:2, which narrates the expulsion of Banu Nadir.
The verse: 'It is He who expelled those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering.'
3
Parse the verse
Identify the components: expulsion (punishment), disbelief (cause), and 'first gathering' (repetition).
The author says expulsion is 'punishment in the sense of killing' and disbelief is 'suitable as a cause'.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Show how each component contributes: the cause (kufr) is extracted, and the repetition indicates that similar cases must be treated similarly.
This is the basis for qiyas: applying the same ruling to new cases with the same cause.
5
Compare with linguistic analogy
The author draws a parallel with metaphor in language, which is permissible by reflecting on realities; similarly, qiyas reflects on causes in law.
This shows the rationality of qiyas.

وقد روينا (۱) ما هو قياس بنفسه من النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. وعمل أصحاب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ورضي الله عنهم في هذا الباب ومناظرتُهم ومشاورتهم في هذا الباب أشهر من أن تخفى على عاقل مميز. فإن طعن طاعن فيهم : فقد ضل عن سواء السبيل، ونابذ الإسلام. ومن ادعى خصوصهم : فقد ادعى أمراً لا دليل عليه، بل الناس سواء في تكليف الاعتبار. وأما المعقول فهو أن الاعتبار واجب بنص القرآن، وهو النظر والتأمل فيما أصاب مَن قَبلنا من المثلات بأسباب نُقلت عنهم ؛ احترازاً عن مثله من الجزاء. وكذلك التأملُ في حقائق اللغة ؛ لاستعارة غيرها لها : سائغ، والقياس نظيره بعينه ؛ لأن الشرع شَرَعَ أحكاماً بمعان أشار إليها، كما أنزل مثلات بأسباب قصها، ودعانا إلى التأمل، ثم الاعتبار. وبيان ذلك في الأصل في قول الله تعالى: ﴿ هُوَ الَّذِي أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا : مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ مِن دِيَرِهِمْ لِأَوَّلِ الْحَشْرِ ﴾ الحشر / 2 : فالإخراج من الديار عقوبةٌ بمعنى القتل، والكفر يصلح داعياً إليه، وأول الحشر دلالة على تكرار هذه العقوبة. (۱) قوله : وقد رُوينا : يعني حديث الخثعمية، وقبلة الصائم... إلى آخر ما تقدم [ ص ١٣٦]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا ظَنَنتُم أَن يَخْرُجُوا ﴾ لله الحشر :/ :۲ دليل على أن إصابة النصرة جزاء التوكل، وقطع الحيل، وأن المَقتُ والخِذْلانَ جزاء النظر إلى القوة والاغترار بالشوكة إلى ما لا يُحصى من معاني النص. ثم دعانا إلى الاعتبار بالتأمل في معاني النص؛ للعمل به فيما لا نص فيه، وكذلك في مسألتنا هذه. وبيان ذلك في مسألة الربا، وذلك أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : الحنطة بالحنطة (۱) : أي بيعوا الحنطة بالحنطة ؛ لأن : الباء : كلمة إلصاق، فدلت على إضمار فعل، مثل قولك: الله. بسم ودلَّ عليه قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام إلا سواء بسواء (٢). (۲) ودلّ عليه حديث عبادة بن الصامت أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب، والورق بالورق إلا سواء بسواء، والحنطة بالحنطة إلا سواء بسواء عَيْناً بعين فمن ،زاد أو استزاد فقد أربى) (۳). (۱) حديث : الحنطة بالحنطة : رواه محمد بن الحسن في «الأصل» من حديث عبادة بلفظ : «الذهب بالذهب مثل بمثل يد بيد والفضة بالفضة مثل بمثل، يد بيد ، والحنطة بالحنطة مثل بمثل، يد بيد». الحديث. وقد رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري بلفظ : الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبُرُّ بالبر، والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح سواء بسواء، مثلاً بمثل، يداً بيد، فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف: فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يداً بيد». (۲) حديث : لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام : تقدم في الحقيقة والمجاز [ص۲۱۹]. (۳) حديث عبادة بن الصامت لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب : تقدم [ص۲۱۹] .
We have narrated (1) that which is qiyas in itself from the Prophet, peace be upon him. And the practice of the Companions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, may Allah be pleased with them, in this chapter, and their debates and consultations in this chapter, are more famous than to be hidden from any intelligent discerning person. So if a critic attacks them, he has strayed from the straight path and renounced Islam. And whoever claims they are unique has claimed something for which there is no evidence; rather, all people are equal in the obligation of consideration. As for the rational (proof), it is that consideration is obligatory by the text of the Qur'an, which is looking and reflecting upon what befell those before us of punishments due to causes transmitted from them, in order to avoid the like of penalty. Similarly, reflection in the realities of language for using metaphor for other things is permissible, and qiyas is its exact parallel; because the law enacted rulings with meanings it indicated, just as it sent down punishments with causes it narrated, and called us to reflection, then consideration. The clarification of this in the original is in the words of Allah Most High: 'It is He who expelled those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering.' [al-Hashr 59:2] Thus expulsion from homes is a punishment in the sense of killing, and disbelief is suitable as a cause for it, and 'first gathering' indicates the repetition of this punishment. (1) (Commentary: 'And we have narrated' means the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, and the kiss of the fasting person... etc. previously on p. 136). And His words: 'You did not think they would leave' (al-Hashr 59:2) is evidence that attaining victory is the reward of trust and cutting off of ruses, and that abhorrence and abandonment are the reward of looking to power and being deluded by might, to countless meanings of the text. Then He called us to consideration by reflecting upon the meanings of the text, to act by it where there is no text, and likewise in this issue of ours. The clarification of this is in the issue of riba, and that is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Wheat for wheat' (1): i.e., sell wheat for wheat, because the ba' (preposition) is a word of adhesion, so it indicates an implied verb, like your saying: 'Bismillah.' And it is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not sell food for food except like for like' (2). And it is supported by the hadith of 'Ubada ibn al-Samit that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not sell gold for gold, nor silver for silver except like for like, and wheat for wheat except like for like, hand to hand; whoever increases or asks for increase has practiced riba' (3). (1) Hadith: 'Wheat for wheat' narrated by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in al-Asl from 'Ubada with the wording: 'Gold for gold like for like hand to hand, silver for silver like for like hand to hand, wheat for wheat like for like hand to hand.' The hadith. And it was narrated by the group except al-Bukhari with the wording: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand; if these types differ, then sell as you wish if it is hand to hand.' (2) Hadith: 'Do not sell food for food' previously in the chapter on haqiqa and majaz [p. 219]. (3) Hadith of 'Ubada: 'Do not sell gold for gold' previously [p. 219].
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a defense of qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a valid source of Islamic law. The author, al-Bazdawi, begins by stating that there is transmitted evidence of qiyas from the Prophet himself, and the practice of the Companions in using qiyas is well-known. He then refutes critics who attack the Companions, saying such criticism is deviation from Islam. He also rejects the claim that the Companions were unique in their ability to use ijtihad; rather, all Muslims are obligated to engage in i'tibar (consideration of causes). The rational proof for qiyas is that the Qur'an commands 'ibar (reflection on past punishments and their causes) to avoid similar fate. This is supported by linguistic analogy: just as metaphor is permissible in language by reflecting on realities, qiyas is permissible in law because the Lawgiver enacted rulings with specific causes (ma'ani). The Qur'anic verse (al-Hashr 59:2) is analyzed: expulsion from homes is a punishment similar to killing, and disbelief is the cause; the phrase 'first gathering' indicates that similar punishments will recur, necessitating consideration of the cause (kufr) to apply similar rulings elsewhere. This establishes the principle of qiyas. The author then applies this to the issue of riba (usury), using hadith that specify exact exchange of wheat, gold, silver, etc., and the principle of equality and hand-to-hand transfer. By understanding the cause ('illa) of riba from these texts, one can analogize to other goods and situations. The passage thus demonstrates that qiyas is firmly rooted in Quranic command and prophetic practice.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared cause ('illa).
اعتبار (i'tibar): Consideration; drawing lessons from past events and their causes to apply to similar situations.
مثلات (mathulat): Exemplary punishments or precedents sent to previous nations as lessons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bazdawi, what does the phrase 'أول الحشر' (first gathering) indicate when proving qiyas?
A) The first expulsion of the People of the Book.
B) That the punishment of expulsion can be repeated.
C) The cause of expulsion is disbelief.
D) The Companions were the first to practice qiyas.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic command to reflect on the causes of past punishments establishes qiyas as an obligatory method of deriving law.

The Prophetic and Companions' Precedent for Qiyas
Proving qiyas from Prophetic and Companions' practice with riba example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the transmitted proofs for qiyas from the Prophet's practice and the Companions' ijtihad, and explain how the riba hadith exemplifies analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
The Prophet himself practiced qiyas and the Companions used it unanimously, making it a sunnah-based source of law.

In this lesson, we examine the transmitted evidence for qiyas: the Prophet's own action, the Companions' widespread practice, and the famous riba hadith. Al-Bazdawi defends the Companions against those who reject their ijtihad, and then provides a concrete case of qiyas from prophetic hadith on usury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The author states that we have narrated qiyas from the Prophet himself.
He references a previously mentioned hadith (al-Khath'amiyyah).
2
Examine the Companions' practice
The Companions' debates and consultations are famous, showing they used qiyas.
The author says this is well-known to any intelligent person.
3
Refute objections
Those who attack the Companions have strayed; those who claim they were unique have no evidence – all people are equal in the obligation of 'ibar.
4
Analyze the riba hadith
The Prophet's statement 'wheat for wheat' and the structural analysis (the preposition ba indicates an implied verb) show the prohibition of riba in wheat with conditions of equality and hand-to-hand.
This is a ruling based on a specific cause.
5
Extract the cause and analogize
From the hadith, the cause is that wheat is a weight/measure-based commodity, and the conditions of like-for-like and hand-to-hand indicate the 'illa. This allows qiyas to other similar goods.
This shows how the Prophet's words provide a model for analogical reasoning.

وقد روينا (۱) ما هو قياس بنفسه من النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام. وعمل أصحاب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ورضي الله عنهم في هذا الباب ومناظرتُهم ومشاورتهم في هذا الباب أشهر من أن تخفى على عاقل مميز. فإن طعن طاعن فيهم : فقد ضل عن سواء السبيل، ونابذ الإسلام. ومن ادعى خصوصهم : فقد ادعى أمراً لا دليل عليه، بل الناس سواء في تكليف الاعتبار. وأما المعقول فهو أن الاعتبار واجب بنص القرآن، وهو النظر والتأمل فيما أصاب مَن قَبلنا من المثلات بأسباب نُقلت عنهم ؛ احترازاً عن مثله من الجزاء. وكذلك التأملُ في حقائق اللغة ؛ لاستعارة غيرها لها : سائغ، والقياس نظيره بعينه ؛ لأن الشرع شَرَعَ أحكاماً بمعان أشار إليها، كما أنزل مثلات بأسباب قصها، ودعانا إلى التأمل، ثم الاعتبار. وبيان ذلك في الأصل في قول الله تعالى: ﴿ هُوَ الَّذِي أَخْرَجَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا : مِنْ أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ مِن دِيَرِهِمْ لِأَوَّلِ الْحَشْرِ ﴾ الحشر / 2 : فالإخراج من الديار عقوبةٌ بمعنى القتل، والكفر يصلح داعياً إليه، وأول الحشر دلالة على تكرار هذه العقوبة. (۱) قوله : وقد رُوينا : يعني حديث الخثعمية، وقبلة الصائم... إلى آخر ما تقدم [ ص ١٣٦]. وقوله تعالى: ﴿ مَا ظَنَنتُم أَن يَخْرُجُوا ﴾ لله الحشر :/ :۲ دليل على أن إصابة النصرة جزاء التوكل، وقطع الحيل، وأن المَقتُ والخِذْلانَ جزاء النظر إلى القوة والاغترار بالشوكة إلى ما لا يُحصى من معاني النص. ثم دعانا إلى الاعتبار بالتأمل في معاني النص؛ للعمل به فيما لا نص فيه، وكذلك في مسألتنا هذه. وبيان ذلك في مسألة الربا، وذلك أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قال : الحنطة بالحنطة (۱) : أي بيعوا الحنطة بالحنطة ؛ لأن : الباء : كلمة إلصاق، فدلت على إضمار فعل، مثل قولك: الله. بسم ودلَّ عليه قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام إلا سواء بسواء (٢). (۲) ودلّ عليه حديث عبادة بن الصامت أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: «لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب، والورق بالورق إلا سواء بسواء، والحنطة بالحنطة إلا سواء بسواء عَيْناً بعين فمن ،زاد أو استزاد فقد أربى) (۳). (۱) حديث : الحنطة بالحنطة : رواه محمد بن الحسن في «الأصل» من حديث عبادة بلفظ : «الذهب بالذهب مثل بمثل يد بيد والفضة بالفضة مثل بمثل، يد بيد ، والحنطة بالحنطة مثل بمثل، يد بيد». الحديث. وقد رواه الجماعة إلا البخاري بلفظ : الذهب بالذهب والفضة بالفضة والبُرُّ بالبر، والشعير بالشعير، والتمر بالتمر، والملح بالملح سواء بسواء، مثلاً بمثل، يداً بيد، فإذا اختلفت هذه الأصناف: فبيعوا كيف شئتم إذا كان يداً بيد». (۲) حديث : لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام : تقدم في الحقيقة والمجاز [ص۲۱۹]. (۳) حديث عبادة بن الصامت لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب : تقدم [ص۲۱۹] .
We have narrated (1) that which is qiyas in itself from the Prophet, peace be upon him. And the practice of the Companions of the Prophet, peace be upon him, may Allah be pleased with them, in this chapter, and their debates and consultations in this chapter, are more famous than to be hidden from any intelligent discerning person. So if a critic attacks them, he has strayed from the straight path and renounced Islam. And whoever claims they are unique has claimed something for which there is no evidence; rather, all people are equal in the obligation of consideration. As for the rational (proof), it is that consideration is obligatory by the text of the Qur'an, which is looking and reflecting upon what befell those before us of punishments due to causes transmitted from them, in order to avoid the like of penalty. Similarly, reflection in the realities of language for using metaphor for other things is permissible, and qiyas is its exact parallel; because the law enacted rulings with meanings it indicated, just as it sent down punishments with causes it narrated, and called us to reflection, then consideration. The clarification of this in the original is in the words of Allah Most High: 'It is He who expelled those who disbelieved from among the People of the Book from their homes at the first gathering.' [al-Hashr 59:2] Thus expulsion from homes is a punishment in the sense of killing, and disbelief is suitable as a cause for it, and 'first gathering' indicates the repetition of this punishment. (1) (Commentary: 'And we have narrated' means the hadith of al-Khath'amiyyah, and the kiss of the fasting person... etc. previously on p. 136). And His words: 'You did not think they would leave' (al-Hashr 59:2) is evidence that attaining victory is the reward of trust and cutting off of ruses, and that abhorrence and abandonment are the reward of looking to power and being deluded by might, to countless meanings of the text. Then He called us to consideration by reflecting upon the meanings of the text, to act by it where there is no text, and likewise in this issue of ours. The clarification of this is in the issue of riba, and that is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Wheat for wheat' (1): i.e., sell wheat for wheat, because the ba' (preposition) is a word of adhesion, so it indicates an implied verb, like your saying: 'Bismillah.' And it is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not sell food for food except like for like' (2). And it is supported by the hadith of 'Ubada ibn al-Samit that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not sell gold for gold, nor silver for silver except like for like, and wheat for wheat except like for like, hand to hand; whoever increases or asks for increase has practiced riba' (3). (1) Hadith: 'Wheat for wheat' narrated by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in al-Asl from 'Ubada with the wording: 'Gold for gold like for like hand to hand, silver for silver like for like hand to hand, wheat for wheat like for like hand to hand.' The hadith. And it was narrated by the group except al-Bukhari with the wording: 'Gold for gold, silver for silver, wheat for wheat, barley for barley, dates for dates, salt for salt, like for like, hand to hand; if these types differ, then sell as you wish if it is hand to hand.' (2) Hadith: 'Do not sell food for food' previously in the chapter on haqiqa and majaz [p. 219]. (3) Hadith of 'Ubada: 'Do not sell gold for gold' previously [p. 219].
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a defense of qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a valid source of Islamic law. The author, al-Bazdawi, begins by stating that there is transmitted evidence of qiyas from the Prophet himself, and the practice of the Companions in using qiyas is well-known. He then refutes critics who attack the Companions, saying such criticism is deviation from Islam. He also rejects the claim that the Companions were unique in their ability to use ijtihad; rather, all Muslims are obligated to engage in i'tibar (consideration of causes). The rational proof for qiyas is that the Qur'an commands 'ibar (reflection on past punishments and their causes) to avoid similar fate. This is supported by linguistic analogy: just as metaphor is permissible in language by reflecting on realities, qiyas is permissible in law because the Lawgiver enacted rulings with specific causes (ma'ani). The Qur'anic verse (al-Hashr 59:2) is analyzed: expulsion from homes is a punishment similar to killing, and disbelief is the cause; the phrase 'first gathering' indicates that similar punishments will recur, necessitating consideration of the cause (kufr) to apply similar rulings elsewhere. This establishes the principle of qiyas. The author then applies this to the issue of riba (usury), using hadith that specify exact exchange of wheat, gold, silver, etc., and the principle of equality and hand-to-hand transfer. By understanding the cause ('illa) of riba from these texts, one can analogize to other goods and situations. The passage thus demonstrates that qiyas is firmly rooted in Quranic command and prophetic practice.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared cause ('illa).
اعتبار (i'tibar): Consideration; drawing lessons from past events and their causes to apply to similar situations.
مثلات (mathulat): Exemplary punishments or precedents sent to previous nations as lessons.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In the riba hadith, which phrase indicates that the prohibition is not limited to the specific goods mentioned but can be extended by qiyas?
A) 'Wheat for wheat'
B) 'Like for like'
C) 'Hand to hand'
D) The analysis of the preposition 'ba' as indicating an implied verb

Key Takeaway
The Prophet and Companions practiced qiyas, and the riba hadith provides a concrete example of how to extract a cause and analogize to new cases.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Deriving the 'Illa for Riba: Capacity and Genus
Derives the effective cause from a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the effective cause ('illa) of riba from the hadith and explain how capacity (qadr) and genus (jins) establish the requirement of equivalence (mumathala).

Core Idea
Riba prohibition hinges on two criteria: capacity (form) and genus (meaning) – quality is irrelevant.

This passage takes you inside the Hanafi method of istinbat – deriving the cause from a text. The hadith 'good and bad are equal' sets the ruling for gold and silver. The author reflects on why equivalence is required, extracting qadr and jins as the motivating factors. Follow along as he unpacks the textual clues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual ruling
The hadith states that in exchange of gold and silver, good and bad are equal. This means quality does not affect equivalence.
The explicit text drops quality as a consideration.
2
Reflect on the motivating factor (dai)
The author asks what drives this requirement of equivalence. The answer is capacity and genus.
Dai is the effective cause that necessitates the ruling.
3
Define capacity
Capacity (qadr) is the fullness of measure, akin to dimensions, establishing form equivalence.
Form equivalence: the items look alike in quantity.
4
Define genus
Genus (jins) is similarity in essence and purpose, establishing meaning equivalence.
Meaning equivalence: the items are of the same type.
5
Drop quality as condition
The hadith and consensus confirm that quality (judah) is not a cause but a condition; its non-existence cannot be a cause.
Distinction between shart (condition) and 'illa (cause) is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التأمل فيما هو داع إلى هذا الحكم مما هو ثابت بهذا النص، وهو إيجاب المماثلة عند البيع بجنسها. وإذا تأملنا وجدنا الداعي إلى هذا الحكم القدر والجنس؛ لأن إيجاب التسوية بين هذه الأموال يقتضي أن تكون أمثالاً متساوية، ولن تكون أمثالاً متساوية إلا بالقدر والجنس؛ لأن كل موجود من موجود بصورته ومعناه، فإنما تقوم المماثلة بهما.
فالقدر: عبارة عن امتلاء المعيار، بمنزلة الطول والعرض، فصار به تحصل المماثلة صورة.
والجنس: عبارة عن مشاكلة المعاني، فتثبت به المماثلة معنى. وسقطت قيمة الجودة بالنص، وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "جيدها ورديئها سواء، تبرها وعينها سواء".
وبالإجماع: فيمن باع قفيزاً جيداً بقفيز رديء وزيادة فلس: أنه لا يصح.
ولما عُرف أن ما لا يُنتفع به إلا بهلاكه فمنفعته في ذاته، ولما صارت أمثالاً بالقدر والجنس، وسقط اعتبار القيمة للجودة شرطاً، لا علة؛ لأن العدم لا يصلح علةً صارت المماثلة ثابتةً بهذين الوصفين، وصار سائر الأعيان فضلاً على هذين المتماثلين بالكيل والجنس بواسطة المماثلة، فصار شرط شيءٍ منها في البيع بمنزلة شرط الخمر، ففسد به البيع.
فهذا أيضاً معقول من هذا النص ليس بثابت بالرأي، فلم يبق من بعد إلا الاعتبار، وهو أنا وجدنا الأرز، والجص، والدخن، وسائر المكيلات والموزونات: أمثالاً متساويةً، فكان الفضلُ على المماثلة فيها فضلاً خالياً العوض في عقد المعاوضة، مثل حكم النص بلا تفاوت، فلزمنا إثباته على طريق الاعتبار، وهو كما ذكرنا من الأمثلة، ما بينها وبين هذه الجملة عن افتراق.
وحصل بما قلنا إثباتُ الأحكام بظواهرها تصديقاً، وإثبات معانيها طمأنينة وشرحاً للصدور وثبت به تعميمُ أحكام النصوص، وفي ذلك تعظيم حدودها.
ولزمنا بهذا الأصل محافظة النصوص بظواهرها ومعانيها ومحافظة ما تضمنته من المعاني التي تعلقت بها أحكامها؛ جمعاً بين الأصول والفروع الحق، وماذا بعد الحقِّ إلا الضلال، وما للخصم إلا التمسك بالجهل.
وصار تعلق الحكم بمعنى من المعاني ثابتاً بحجةٍ فيها ضَرْبُ شبهة، وفي التعيين احتمال وجائز وضع الأسباب للعمل على هذا الوجه، كالنصوص المحتملة بصيغها من الكتاب والسنة.
وصار الكتاب تبياناً لكل شيء من هذا الوجه؛ لأن ما ثبت بالقياس يُضاف إليه، فكان أولى من العمل بالحال التي ليست بحجة، فإذا تعذر العمل بالقياس صِيْرَ إلى الحال وثبت أن طاعة الله تعالى لا تتوقف على علم اليقين والله أعلم.
Reflection on what is the motivating factor for this ruling, which is established by this text, and it is the requirement of equivalence when selling with its genus. And when we reflect, we find the motivating factor for this ruling is capacity and genus; because the requirement of equality between these goods necessitates that they be equal equivalents, and they will not be equal equivalents except by capacity and genus; because every existent exists by its form and meaning, so equivalence is established by them. So capacity: it is an expression of the fullness of the measure, akin to length and width, thus equivalence in form is achieved. And genus: it is an expression of the similarity of meanings, thus equivalence in meaning is established. And the value of quality is dropped by the text, which is his saying, peace be upon him: "Its good and bad are equal, its gold nugget and its coin are equal." And by consensus: regarding one who sells a good qafiz for a bad qafiz and an extra fils: that it is not valid. And since it is known that that which is only benefited from by its destruction, its benefit is in its essence, and since they become equivalents by capacity and genus, and consideration of value for quality is dropped as a condition, not a cause; because non-existence cannot be a cause, equivalence becomes established by these two descriptions, and the rest of the commodities become extra over these two that are equivalent by measure and genus by means of equivalence, so stipulating something of them in a sale becomes like stipulating wine, so the sale is corrupted by it. So this too is intelligible from this text, not established by opinion, so nothing remains after that except analogical reasoning, which is that we found rice, gypsum, millet, and all other measured and weighed items to be equal equivalents, so the excess over equivalence in them is an excess devoid of compensation in a compensatory contract, like the ruling of the text without distinction, so we are obliged to establish it by way of analogy, as we mentioned from examples, between them and this general statement there is no difference. And what we have said achieves establishing rulings by their apparent meanings as confirmation, and establishing their meanings as tranquility and expansion of the breast, and by it the generalization of the rulings of texts is established, and in that is the veneration of their boundaries. And by this principle we are obliged to preserve the texts by their apparent meanings and their meanings, and to preserve what they contain of meanings to which their rulings are attached; combining the principles and the derived rulings in truth, and what after truth is there but misguidance, and the opponent has nothing but clinging to ignorance. And the attachment of the ruling to a meaning is established by an evidence that contains a kind of probability, and in specification there is possibility, and it is permissible to place causes for action in this manner, like texts that are probable in their wording from the Book and Sunnah. And the Book became an exposition of everything from this perspective; because what is established by analogy is attributed to it, so it is more appropriate than acting upon the state that is not evidence, and if acting by analogy becomes impossible, then one turns to the state, and it is established that obedience to Allah Most High does not depend on certain knowledge. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a detailed derivation (istinbat) of the riba ruling from the hadith 'Good and bad are equal' regarding gold and silver. The author, likely from the Hanafi tradition, explains that the motivating factor (dai) for the prohibition of excess in ribawi items is two-fold: capacity (qadr) for form equivalence and genus (jins) for meaning equivalence. Quality (judah) is dropped as a condition (shart) not a cause (illah), because non-existence of quality cannot be a cause. Thus, in a sale of like-for-like, any excess is like a stipulation of wine, invalidating the sale. The reasoning then extends via qiyas (analogy) to all measured and weighed items, such as rice, gypsum, and millet, establishing that any excess without compensation is prohibited. The author emphasizes that this derivation is from the text, not personal opinion, and upholds the principles of preserving both the literal and intended meanings of the texts. The passage concludes with a defense of qiyas as a valid method and notes that when qiyas is impossible, one may resort to the apparent state (hal). This is classic Hanafi usul: deriving rulings through causal reasoning from explicit proofs.

Key Terms
القدر (al-qadr): The measure (capacity) by which items are quantified, like fullness of a measure, akin to length and width.
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or type of an item, signifying similarity in essence and purpose.
المماثلة (al-mumathala): Equivalence in both form (qadr) and meaning (jins) required in ribawi sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the value of quality (qimat al-judah) dropped as a consideration in determining equivalence in riba according to this passage?
A) Because quality is intangible.
B) Because the hadith explicitly says 'good and bad are equal', and non-existence cannot be a cause.
C) Because qiyas requires ignoring quality.
D) Because quality is too subjective.

Key Takeaway
The effective cause for riba prohibition is capacity and genus; quality is irrelevant.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas from Gold and Silver to All Measured Items
Extends ruling via qiyas to all measured items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply qiyas to extend the riba ruling to other measured and weighed items using the derived 'illa of capacity and genus.

Core Idea
Qiyas generalizes the riba prohibition to all items sharing the cause of capacity and genus.

The author moves from the explicit text to analogical reasoning. Having identified qadr and jins as the cause, he argues that all measured and weighed items (like rice, gypsum, millet) fall under the same ruling. Follow the analogical extension step by step.

Guided Path
1
Recall the original ruling
Gold and silver must be equal in capacity and genus when exchanged.
This is the asl (original case).
2
Identify the 'illa
The 'illa is capacity (measure) and genus.
These are the effective causes.
3
Test the analogy
Other items like rice and gypsum are also measured/weighed and of the same genus when exchanged.
The 'illa is present in the far' (new case).
4
Confirm no distinction
The author says there is no difference between the examples and the general statement.
No valid distinction (fasl) exists.
5
Conclude the ruling
Any excess in such sales is prohibited riba.
The hukm is transferred.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التأمل فيما هو داع إلى هذا الحكم مما هو ثابت بهذا النص، وهو إيجاب المماثلة عند البيع بجنسها. وإذا تأملنا وجدنا الداعي إلى هذا الحكم القدر والجنس؛ لأن إيجاب التسوية بين هذه الأموال يقتضي أن تكون أمثالاً متساوية، ولن تكون أمثالاً متساوية إلا بالقدر والجنس؛ لأن كل موجود من موجود بصورته ومعناه، فإنما تقوم المماثلة بهما.
فالقدر: عبارة عن امتلاء المعيار، بمنزلة الطول والعرض، فصار به تحصل المماثلة صورة.
والجنس: عبارة عن مشاكلة المعاني، فتثبت به المماثلة معنى. وسقطت قيمة الجودة بالنص، وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "جيدها ورديئها سواء، تبرها وعينها سواء".
وبالإجماع: فيمن باع قفيزاً جيداً بقفيز رديء وزيادة فلس: أنه لا يصح.
ولما عُرف أن ما لا يُنتفع به إلا بهلاكه فمنفعته في ذاته، ولما صارت أمثالاً بالقدر والجنس، وسقط اعتبار القيمة للجودة شرطاً، لا علة؛ لأن العدم لا يصلح علةً صارت المماثلة ثابتةً بهذين الوصفين، وصار سائر الأعيان فضلاً على هذين المتماثلين بالكيل والجنس بواسطة المماثلة، فصار شرط شيءٍ منها في البيع بمنزلة شرط الخمر، ففسد به البيع.
فهذا أيضاً معقول من هذا النص ليس بثابت بالرأي، فلم يبق من بعد إلا الاعتبار، وهو أنا وجدنا الأرز، والجص، والدخن، وسائر المكيلات والموزونات: أمثالاً متساويةً، فكان الفضلُ على المماثلة فيها فضلاً خالياً العوض في عقد المعاوضة، مثل حكم النص بلا تفاوت، فلزمنا إثباته على طريق الاعتبار، وهو كما ذكرنا من الأمثلة، ما بينها وبين هذه الجملة عن افتراق.
وحصل بما قلنا إثباتُ الأحكام بظواهرها تصديقاً، وإثبات معانيها طمأنينة وشرحاً للصدور وثبت به تعميمُ أحكام النصوص، وفي ذلك تعظيم حدودها.
ولزمنا بهذا الأصل محافظة النصوص بظواهرها ومعانيها ومحافظة ما تضمنته من المعاني التي تعلقت بها أحكامها؛ جمعاً بين الأصول والفروع الحق، وماذا بعد الحقِّ إلا الضلال، وما للخصم إلا التمسك بالجهل.
وصار تعلق الحكم بمعنى من المعاني ثابتاً بحجةٍ فيها ضَرْبُ شبهة، وفي التعيين احتمال وجائز وضع الأسباب للعمل على هذا الوجه، كالنصوص المحتملة بصيغها من الكتاب والسنة.
وصار الكتاب تبياناً لكل شيء من هذا الوجه؛ لأن ما ثبت بالقياس يُضاف إليه، فكان أولى من العمل بالحال التي ليست بحجة، فإذا تعذر العمل بالقياس صِيْرَ إلى الحال وثبت أن طاعة الله تعالى لا تتوقف على علم اليقين والله أعلم.
Reflection on what is the motivating factor for this ruling, which is established by this text, and it is the requirement of equivalence when selling with its genus. And when we reflect, we find the motivating factor for this ruling is capacity and genus; because the requirement of equality between these goods necessitates that they be equal equivalents, and they will not be equal equivalents except by capacity and genus; because every existent exists by its form and meaning, so equivalence is established by them. So capacity: it is an expression of the fullness of the measure, akin to length and width, thus equivalence in form is achieved. And genus: it is an expression of the similarity of meanings, thus equivalence in meaning is established. And the value of quality is dropped by the text, which is his saying, peace be upon him: "Its good and bad are equal, its gold nugget and its coin are equal." And by consensus: regarding one who sells a good qafiz for a bad qafiz and an extra fils: that it is not valid. And since it is known that that which is only benefited from by its destruction, its benefit is in its essence, and since they become equivalents by capacity and genus, and consideration of value for quality is dropped as a condition, not a cause; because non-existence cannot be a cause, equivalence becomes established by these two descriptions, and the rest of the commodities become extra over these two that are equivalent by measure and genus by means of equivalence, so stipulating something of them in a sale becomes like stipulating wine, so the sale is corrupted by it. So this too is intelligible from this text, not established by opinion, so nothing remains after that except analogical reasoning, which is that we found rice, gypsum, millet, and all other measured and weighed items to be equal equivalents, so the excess over equivalence in them is an excess devoid of compensation in a compensatory contract, like the ruling of the text without distinction, so we are obliged to establish it by way of analogy, as we mentioned from examples, between them and this general statement there is no difference. And what we have said achieves establishing rulings by their apparent meanings as confirmation, and establishing their meanings as tranquility and expansion of the breast, and by it the generalization of the rulings of texts is established, and in that is the veneration of their boundaries. And by this principle we are obliged to preserve the texts by their apparent meanings and their meanings, and to preserve what they contain of meanings to which their rulings are attached; combining the principles and the derived rulings in truth, and what after truth is there but misguidance, and the opponent has nothing but clinging to ignorance. And the attachment of the ruling to a meaning is established by an evidence that contains a kind of probability, and in specification there is possibility, and it is permissible to place causes for action in this manner, like texts that are probable in their wording from the Book and Sunnah. And the Book became an exposition of everything from this perspective; because what is established by analogy is attributed to it, so it is more appropriate than acting upon the state that is not evidence, and if acting by analogy becomes impossible, then one turns to the state, and it is established that obedience to Allah Most High does not depend on certain knowledge. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage is a detailed derivation (istinbat) of the riba ruling from the hadith 'Good and bad are equal' regarding gold and silver. The author, likely from the Hanafi tradition, explains that the motivating factor (dai) for the prohibition of excess in ribawi items is two-fold: capacity (qadr) for form equivalence and genus (jins) for meaning equivalence. Quality (judah) is dropped as a condition (shart) not a cause (illah), because non-existence of quality cannot be a cause. Thus, in a sale of like-for-like, any excess is like a stipulation of wine, invalidating the sale. The reasoning then extends via qiyas (analogy) to all measured and weighed items, such as rice, gypsum, and millet, establishing that any excess without compensation is prohibited. The author emphasizes that this derivation is from the text, not personal opinion, and upholds the principles of preserving both the literal and intended meanings of the texts. The passage concludes with a defense of qiyas as a valid method and notes that when qiyas is impossible, one may resort to the apparent state (hal). This is classic Hanafi usul: deriving rulings through causal reasoning from explicit proofs.

Key Terms
القدر (al-qadr): The measure (capacity) by which items are quantified, like fullness of a measure, akin to length and width.
الجنس (al-jins): The genus or type of an item, signifying similarity in essence and purpose.
المماثلة (al-mumathala): Equivalence in both form (qadr) and meaning (jins) required in ribawi sales.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which of the following is NOT an example given in the passage for qiyas extension?
A) Rice
B) Gypsum
C) Millet
D) Gold

Key Takeaway
Qiyas from gold/silver extends the riba prohibition to all measured/weighed items sharing the 'illa of capacity and genus.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Iʿtibār: The Inevitable Extension of Textual Rulings
Concluding argument for the validity of qiyas based on textual and rational evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul considers qiyas (iʿtibār) a necessary method derived from the text, not mere opinion, and illustrate this with the example of riba in weighables.

Core Idea
Qiyas is the text's meaning extended by necessary analogy, not arbitrary opinion.

This passage concludes a defense of analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Islamic legal theory. It argues that once explicit textual evidence is exhausted, the only valid method to derive rulings is iʿtibār — comparing new cases to textual rulings based on shared meaning. The author uses the example of riba in measurable commodities to show that qiyas is not arbitrary opinion but a logical extension of the text itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Claim
Locate the statement that after textual evidence, nothing remains except iʿtibār. Understand that iʿtibār is synonymous with qiyas (analogical reasoning) and is presented as the only valid method beyond direct nass.
iʿtibār literally means 'consideration' or 'taking into account'; in usul it refers to deriving rulings by comparing cases.
2
Examine the Example
The author lists rice, plaster, and panic grass as measurable/weighable items. The ruling being analogized is the prohibition of riba: any excess over equality in exchange is forbidden, just as in the explicit textual cases.
The textual basis is the hadith on the six commodities (gold, silver, wheat, barley, dates, salt) where equality is required.
3
Analyze the Logic of Analogy
The author argues that this analogy is derived from the text, not opinion. The effective cause (ʿillah) is measurability/weight, which is implicitly present in the textual examples. By extending this ʿillah to new items, the ruling is preserved without introducing new legislation.
Hanafis consider the ʿillah as the textual meaning that allows generalization.
4
Understand the Dual Preservation
The author emphasizes preserving both the apparent meanings (ẓawāhir) and the underlying meanings (maʿānī) of the texts. This ensures that both the letter and the spirit of the law are maintained, combining usul and furu‘ in truth.
This dual preservation is a hallmark of Hanafi methodology.
5
Address the Opponent's Stance
The opponent (likely those rejecting qiyas) is dismissed as clinging to ignorance. The author asserts that even probabilistic texts are relied upon, so qiyas, which is attributed to the Book, is even more valid. If qiyas is impossible, one resorts to istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity).
Obedience to Allah does not require certain knowledge in every case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا أيضاً معقول من هذا النص ليس بثابت بالرأي، فلم يبق من بعد إلا الاعتبار، وهو أنا وجدنا الأرز، والجص، والدخن، وسائر المكيلات والموزونات : أمثالاً متساويةً، فكان الفضلُ على المماثلة فيها : فضلاً خالياً العوض في عقد المعاوضة، مثل حكم النص بلا تفاوت، فلزمنا إثباته على طريق الاعتبار، وهو كما ذكرنا من الأمثلة، ما بينها وبين هذه الجملة عن افتراق وحصل بما قلنا إثباتُ الأحكام بظواهرها تصديقاً، وإثبات معانيها وطمأنينة وشرحاً للصدور وثبت به تعميمُ أحكام النصوص، وفي ذلك تعظيم حدودها. ولزمنا بهذا الأصل محافظة النصوص بظواهرها ومعانيها ومحافظة ما تضمنته من المعاني التي تعلقت بها أحكامها؛ جمعاً بين الأصول والفروع الحق، وماذا بعد الحقِّ إلا الضلال، وما للخصم إلا التمسك معاً، وهو بالجهل. وصار تعلق الحكم بمعنى من المعاني ثابتاً بحجةٍ فيها ضَرْبُ شبهة ، وفي التعيين احتمال وجائز وضع الأسباب للعمل على هذا الوجه، كالنصوص المحتملة بصيغها من الكتاب والسنة. وصار الكتاب تبياناً لكل شيء من هذا الوجه ؛ لأن ما ثبت بالقياس : يُضاف إليه، فكان أولى من العمل بالحال التي ليست بحجة، فإذا تعذر العمل بالقياس : صِيْرَ إلى الحال وثبت أن طاعة الله تعالى لا تتوقف على علم اليقين والله أعلم.
So this is also understood from this text, not established by opinion. Nothing remains thereafter except iʿtibār (analogical consideration), and it is that we found rice, plaster, panic grass, and all measurable and weighable items to be equal equivalents, so excess over equality in them is a consideration free of compensation in a contract of exchange, like the ruling of the text without disparity. Therefore, we are obliged to establish it by the way of iʿtibār, as we mentioned from the examples, between them and this sentence concerning separation. And by what we said, the establishment of rulings by their apparent meanings as verification, and the establishment of their meanings, tranquility, and expansion of breasts, and by it the generalization of the rulings of texts is established, and in that is the magnification of their boundaries. And by this principle we are obliged to preserve the texts by their apparent meanings and their intended meanings, and to preserve what they contain of meanings to which their rulings are attached; combining the principles and the branches in truth. And what is after truth except misguidance, and the opponent has nothing but clinging together, and it is ignorance. And the attachment of a ruling to a meaning among meanings became established by an evidence that contains a kind of uncertainty, and in specification there is probability, and it is permissible to posit causes for action in this manner, like texts that are probabilistically worded from the Book and Sunna. And the Book became an explanation of everything in this respect, because what is established by qiyas is attributed to it, so it is more appropriate than acting upon the state that is not an evidence. And when acting upon qiyas becomes impossible, one turns to the state, and it is established that obedience to Allah Almighty does not depend on certain knowledge. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage concludes an argument defending the use of analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Islamic law. The author begins by stating that the ruling under discussion is understood from the text, not from mere opinion. After textual evidence, the only remaining method is iʿtibār (analogical consideration). The author gives examples of items like rice, plaster, and panic grass, which are all measurable/weighable commodities. In such items, equality is required in exchange; any excess without compensation is ribā (usury), analogous to the explicit textual ruling. This analogy is not based on arbitrary opinion but is derived from the text's own indications. The passage then emphasizes that rulings are established both by the apparent meaning (ẓāhir) and by the underlying meanings (maʿānī) of the texts. This dual preservation ensures that both the letter and spirit of the law are maintained. The opponent (likely those who reject qiyas) has no valid argument except clinging to ignorance. The author also addresses that the connection between a ruling and its meaning may involve some uncertainty (shubha), but that is acceptable because even probabilistic texts from the Qur'an and Sunna are relied upon. Ultimately, the Qur'an is a clarification for everything in this regard, because qiyas is attributed to it. If qiyas is impossible, one may resort to the original state (al-ḥāl, i.e., istiṣḥāb). Obedience to Allah does not require certain knowledge (ʿilm al-yaqīn) in every case.

Key Terms
الاعتبار (al-iʿtibār): Analogical consideration; deriving a ruling by comparing an unregulated case to a regulated one based on a shared effective cause (ʿillah).
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (farʿ) due to a shared ʿillah.
النص (al-naṣṣ): The explicit textual evidence from Qur'an or Sunna that provides a clear ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the remaining method after textual evidence when deriving a ruling?
A) Personal opinion (ra'y)
B) Istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity)
C) Iʿtibār (analogical consideration)
D) Taqlid (blind following)

Key Takeaway
Iʿtibār (analogical reasoning) is a necessary method derived from textual meanings, not personal opinion, and is used to extend rulings to new cases based on shared effective causes.

Dispute on the Taʿlīl of the Uṣūl
Presentation of four scholarly opinions on taʿlīl al-uṣūl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four scholarly opinions on taʿlīl al-uṣūl and identify the Hanafi position, including its requirements for specification evidence and evidence for the present case.

Core Idea
Hanafis: uṣūl are manifestly caused unless prevented, but need specification evidence.

This passage opens a crucial usul al-fiqh discussion: are the original rulings (uṣūl) in the sacred texts inherently caused by specific attributes (ʿillah)? Four distinct positions are presented, with the Hanafi view being the fourth. Understanding these positions is essential for grasping how qiyās operates and where the schools differ. The example of gold and silver in ribā illustrates the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Enumerate the four opinions
Read the passage and list each of the four positions on whether uṣūl are ʿillah. Note the key phrase for each: 'غير شاهدة', 'معلولة بكل وصف', 'لا بدَّ من دليل مميز', and 'معلولة شاهدة إلا بمانع'.
Memorize the Arabic labels for each opinion.
2
Understand the Shafiʿi-like position
Identify which opinion is ascribed to Imam al-Shafiʿi (the third). Note that it requires a distinguishing evidence (dalīl mumayyiz).
The text says 'وهذا أشبه بمذهب الشافعي'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi position
Focus on the fourth opinion (قولنا). The Hanafis hold that uṣūl are 'shāhida' – manifestly causal – unless prevented. But this is conditional: there must be evidence of specification and prior evidence that the cause applies to the present case.
'شاهدة' implies the ʿillah is apparent, but not without verification.
4
Examine the example
The passage gives the dispute over gold and silver: Hanafis use weight as ʿillah; al-Shafiʿi rejects that and requires specific textual evidence.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical consequence.
5
Evaluate the first group's argument
The first group argues that the text's wording is operative, and transferring the ruling to a meaning via taʿlīl is like leaving the literal for metaphorical, which needs strong evidence. They also note attributes conflict, making universal taʿlīl impossible.
This argument challenges the very possibility of taʿlīl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تعليل الأصول واختلفوا في هذه الأصول: فقال بعضُهم : هي غيرُ شاهدة، أي غيرُ معلولة إلا بدليل. وقال بعضُهم : هي معلولةٌ بكل وصف يُمكن إلا بمانع. وقال بعضُهم : هي معلولةٌ لكن لا بدَّ من دليل مميز، وهذا أشبه بمذهب الشافعي رحمه الله. والقول الرابع قولنا إنا نقول هي معلولة شاهدة إلا بمانع ولا بدَّ من دلالة التمييز، ولا بد قبل ذلك من قيام الدليل على أنه للحال ومثال :هذا اختلافنا في تعليل الذهب والفضة بالوزن. وأنكر الشافعي رحمه الله التعليل بالوزن، فلا يصح الاستدلال بأن في الأصل معلولةٌ إلا بإقامة الدليل في هذا النص على الخصوص أنه معلول. احتج أهلُ المقالة الأولى بأن النص موجب بصيغته، وبالتعليل ينتقل حكمه إلى معناه، وذلك كالمجاز من الحقيقة، فلا يُترك إلا بدليل. ألا يُرى أن الأوصاف متعارضة، والتعليلَ بالكل غير ممكن، وبكل
Chapter on the taʿlīl (causation) of the principles. And they differed concerning these principles: Some said: They are not shahida (manifestly causal), i.e., not known to be ʿillah except by evidence. And some said: They are ʿillah by every possible attribute except when there is a preventer. And some said: They are ʿillah, but a distinguishing evidence is necessary, and this is closer to the madhhab of al-Shafiʿi, may Allah have mercy on him. And the fourth saying is our saying: We say they are ʿillah manifestly except when there is a preventer, and evidence of specification is necessary, and before that there must be evidence that it is for the present case. And an example of this is our difference concerning the taʿlīl of gold and silver by weight. And al-Shafiʿi, may Allah have mercy on him, denied taʿlīl by weight, so it is not valid to argue that the original case is ʿillah except by adducing evidence in this text specifically that it is ʿillah. The proponents of the first group argued that the text is operative by its wording, and by taʿlīl its ruling is transferred to its meaning, and that is like metaphor (majāz) from reality (ḥaqīqah), so it should not be abandoned except with evidence. Do you not see that attributes are contradictory, and taʿlīl by everything is impossible, and by every...
Source pages p. 566

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on the taʿlīl (causation) of the uṣūl (the original rulings of primary texts). The author presents four scholarly opinions: (1) The uṣūl are not known to be caused (ʿillah) unless there is explicit evidence (i.e., they are not inherently ʿillah). (2) They are ʿillah by every possible attribute unless there is a preventer (i.e., any suitable attribute could be the cause unless blocked). (3) They are ʿillah but require a distinguishing evidence (dālīl mumayyiz) to specify which attribute is the cause; this is attributed to Imam al-Shafiʿi. (4) The Hanafi position: They are ʿillah and manifestly (shāhida) so, unless prevented, but they need evidence of specification (dalālat al-tamyīz) and prior evidence that the cause applies to the present case. The example given is the dispute over gold and silver: Hanafis consider weight as the ʿillah for ribā, while al-Shafiʿi rejects that and requires specific textual evidence to show that the original case is indeed ʿillah. The argument of the first group is that the text operates by its wording, and taʿlīl transfers the ruling to the meaning, similar to metaphor, so it should not be abandoned without evidence. The passage ends abruptly, emphasizing the difficulty of conflicting attributes and the impossibility of universal taʿlīl.

Key Terms
التعليل (al-taʿlīl): The process of identifying the effective cause (ʿillah) that grounds a legal ruling in an original text (aṣl).
الأصل (al-aṣl): The original case or primary text from which a ruling is derived; the source of the analogy.
شاهدة (shāhida): Manifestly causal; an attribute that is evident and clearly considered the ʿillah without needing extensive proof.
دليل مميز (dalīl mumayyiz): A distinguishing evidence that specifies which attribute among many is the effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the taʿlīl of the uṣūl as presented in this passage?
A) The uṣūl are not ʿillah except with explicit evidence.
B) The uṣūl are ʿillah by every possible attribute unless prevented.
C) The uṣūl are ʿillah manifestly unless prevented, but need evidence of specification and evidence for the present case.
D) Taʿlīl is completely rejected.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position on taʿlīl al-uṣūl is that they are manifestly causal (shāhida) unless prevented, but require both specification evidence and evidence for the present case.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Dispute on Ta'lil: All Attributes or Only Proved One?
Dispute over whether all attributes of a text are suitable for ta'lil in qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on ta'lil, explain its requirement for a distinguishing evidence (dalīl al-tamyīz), and evaluate the opposing argument based on analogy with hadith narration.

Core Idea
Ta'lil in qiyas requires specific evidence; not all attributes of a text are valid causes without proof.

This passage presents a fundamental dispute in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: can any attribute of a text serve as the effective cause ('illah) for qiyas, or must there be evidence that specifically identifies the cause? The author examines three views, defending the Hanafi insistence on a distinguishing evidence (dalīl al-tamyīz). The key issue is whether probability (ihtimal) alone suffices to establish a text as 'caused' (ma'lul) when some texts are not. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to perform sound qiyas and avoid arbitrary reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage to distinguish the three views: (1) the opposing school that holds all attributes valid unless a preventing factor exists, (2) the view that ta'lil cannot apply to all attributes because it would block qiyas, and (3) the Hanafi position requiring a distinguishing evidence.
Note that the 'second school' in the text is the opponent; the 'third view' is a separate intermediate position.
2
Analyze the opponent's analogy
The opponent argues by analogy with hadith narration: just as every trustworthy narrator's report is accepted unless impeached, here every attribute is a potential cause unless a preventing factor exists. Identify the structure of this analogy and its claimed basis.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response points out a critical difference: in hadith, the proof is the narration itself, not the attributes of the narrator. Here, probability affects the very basis of the proof—whether the text is caused or not. The Law sometimes suspends (waqf) and sometimes deduces (istinbat), so both are principles; accepting all attributes would ignore this balance.
Note the reference to istishab al-hal: a state is presumed to continue unless proven otherwise.
4
Understand the need for distinguishing evidence
The author argues that texts are of two types: caused and uncaused. Without evidence, we cannot know which type a text belongs to. Therefore, a dalīl al-tamyīz is necessary to establish that the text is caused and to identify which attribute is the 'illah.
The term 'dalīl al-tamyīz' is central to the Hanafi position.
5
Apply to the riba example
The author provides an example from gold and silver riba. The text's ruling is caused due to weight/measure, proven by the hadith 'hand in hand' and the prohibition of nasi'ah. This shows how distinguishing evidence is used in practice.
This example illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical consequence of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصف محتمل، فكان الوقف أصلاً.
واحتج أهل المقالة الثانية بأن الشرع لما جعل القياس حجة، ولا حجة إلا بأن تجعل أوصافُ النص علةً وشهادةً صارت الأوصاف يصير كلها صالحةً، فصلح الإثبات بكل وصف إلا بمانع.
مثل رواية الحديث لما كان حجة، والاجتماع متعذر : صارت رواية
كل عدل حجةٌ لا تُترك إلا بمانع، فكذلك هذا.
ولما صار القياس دليلاً صار التعليل والشهادة من النص أصلاً، فلا يُترك بالاحتمال، وإنما التعليل لإثبات حكم الفروع، فأما النص فيبقى موجباً كما كان. ووجه القول الثالث: أنه لما ثبت القول بالتعليل، وصار ذلك أصلاً بطل التعليلُ بكل الأوصاف؛ لأنه ما شرع إلا للقياس مرةً، وللحجر أخرى عند الشافعي رحمه الله ، وهذا يَسُدُّ باب القياس أصلاً، فوجب التعليل بواحد من الجملة فلا بدَّ من دليل يوجب التمييز؛ لأن التعليل بالمجهول باطل والواحد من الجملة هو المتيقن بعد سقوط الجملة، لكنه مجهول.
وقلنا نحن إن دليل التمييز شرط على ما نبيّن إن شاء الله تعالى
لكنا نحتاج قبل ذلك إلى قيام الدلالة على كون الأصل شاهداً للحال؛ لأنا قد وجدنا من النصوص ما هو غير معلول فاحتمل هذا أن يكون من تلك الجملة، لكنَّ هذا الأصل لم يسقط بالاحتمال، ولم يبق حجةً على غيره، وهو الفرع بالاحتمال أيضاً على مثال استصحاب الحال.
ولا يلزم عليه أن الاقتداء بالنبي عليه الصلاة والسلام واجب مع قيام الاختصاص في بعض الأمور ؛ لأن الاقتداء بالنبي عليه الصلاة والسلام إنما صار واجباً لكونه رسولاً وإماماً صادقاً، وهذا لا شبهة فيه، فلم يسقط العمل بما دخل من الاحتمال في نفس العمل فأما ها هنا فإن النصوص نوعان: معلول وغير معلول، فيصير الاحتمال واقعاً في نفس الحجة، ولأن الشرع ابتلانا بالوقف مرة وبالاستنباط أخرى، كل ذلك أصل، فلما اعتدلا : لم يستقم الاكتفاء بأحد الأصلين.
فأما الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام فإنما بعث للاقتداء به، لا معارض لذلك، فلا يبطل بالاحتمال.
ومثال هذا الأصل: قولنا في الذهب والفضة: إن حكم النص في ذلك معلول، فلا يُسمع منا الاستدلال بالأصل، وأن التعليل أصل في النصوص، بل لا بدَّ من إقامة الدلالة على أن هذا النص بعينه معلول، ودلالة ذلك أن هذا النص تضمَّن حكم التعيين بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «يداً بيد»، وذلك من باب الربا أيضاً.
ألا يُرى أن تعيين أحد البدلين شرط جواز كل بيع ؛ احترازاً عن الدين بالدين وتعيين البدل الآخر واجب ؛ طلباً للتسوية بينهما؛ احترازاً عن شبهة الفضل الذي هو رباً.
وقد قال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إنما الربا في النسيئة»، وقد وجدنا هذا الحكم متعدياً عنه حتى قال الشافعي رحمه الله في بيع الطعام (١) فصل : قوله : بقوله يدا بيد : هو في حديث عبادة عند محمد «الأصل». (٢) حديث : إنما الربا في النسيئة : متفق عليه من حديث أسامة بن زيد.
A probable description, so the suspension was an original [principle]. The proponents of the second school argued that since the Law made analogy a proof, and there is no proof except by making the attributes of the text a cause and a testimony, the attributes all become valid, so proof by every attribute is valid except prevented by an impediment. Like the narration of hadith being a proof, and meeting [directly] is impossible: the narration of every just [person] became a proof not abandoned except due to an impediment, so likewise this. And when analogy became a proof, making [one attribute] a cause and testimony from the text became an original [principle], so it is not abandoned due to probability. Ta'lil is only to prove the ruling of branches, but the text remains operative as it was. The face of the third view: when ta'lil was established and became an original, ta'lil by all attributes is invalidated; because it was legislated only for qiyas at one time, and for restriction at another according to al-Shafi'i, and this blocks the door of qiyas entirely. So ta'lil by one of the totality is obligatory, and an evidence that necessitates distinction is indispensable; because ta'lil by the unknown is false, and the one from the totality is the certain after the fall of the totality, but it is unknown. And we said that the evidence of distinction is a condition, as we will explain God willing. But we need before that to establish the indication that the original is a witness for the case; because we have found among the texts what is not caused, so it is probable that this [text] is from that group. But this original did not fall due to probability, and it remains a proof for others? That is the branch also by probability on the example of istishab al-hal. And it does not necessitate that following the Prophet is obligatory despite the existence of specificity in some matters; because following the Prophet became obligatory due to his being a messenger and a truthful imam, and there is no doubt about this, so action is not invalidated by probability entering into the action itself. But here the texts are of two types: caused and uncaused, so probability occurs in the proof itself. And because the Law tested us with suspension once and with deduction another time, each is an original. When they are balanced, it is not sound to suffice with one of the two originals. As for the Messenger, he was sent to be followed, with no opposition to that, so it is not invalidated by probability. An example of this original: our saying concerning gold and silver: the ruling of the text concerning them is caused, so the deduction by the original is not accepted from us, and ta'lil is an original in texts, rather it is necessary to establish the indication that this very text is caused. The proof of that is that this text includes the ruling of specification by his saying: 'hand in hand', and that is from the chapter of riba as well. Do you not see that specification of one of the two counter-values is a condition of validity of every sale, as a precaution against debt for debt, and specification of the other counter-value is obligatory, seeking equality between them, as a precaution against the suspicion of excess which is riba. And the Prophet said: 'Riba is only in nasi'ah', and we have found this ruling transmissible from it until al-Shafi'i said concerning the sale of food... (1) Section: His saying: 'hand in hand' is in the hadith of Ubadah according to Muhammad in al-Asl. (2) Hadith: 'Riba is only in nasi'ah' is agreed upon from the hadith of Usamah ibn Zayd.
Source pages p. 567

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh regarding the method of identifying the 'illah (cause) for qiyas. The author presents three positions. The first (the second school mentioned) argues that since qiyas is a proof, and proof requires making attributes of the text into causes, all attributes are valid unless a preventing factor exists, analogous to hadith narration where every reliable narrator's report is accepted unless there is an impediment. The second (third view) argues that if ta'lil is established, it cannot apply to all attributes because then all texts would be caused, which blocks qiyas; instead, only one attribute from a totality must be chosen, but it remains unknown without evidence. The Hanafi position (the author's) is that ta'lil requires a distinguishing evidence (dalil tamyiz); it is not sufficient that all attributes are potentially valid. The author argues that we must first establish that the original text is actually caused; some texts are not caused, so not every text is suitable for ta'lil. He addresses an objection about following the Prophet despite specificity: following the Prophet is obligatory without doubt, but here probability affects the proof itself, not just the action, because texts can be either caused or uncaused. He then gives an example: the ruling on gold and silver riba is caused (due to weight and measure), and the proof that it is caused is the explicit text requiring hand-to-hand exchange and the prohibition of nasi'ah. The text concludes with a reference to al-Shafi'i's opinion on food sales, indicating the transmissibility of the 'illah.

Key Terms
التعليل (al-ta‘līl): The process of identifying the effective cause ('illah) from a text to extend its ruling to new cases via qiyas.
الوصف (al-waṣf): An attribute or description of a text that could potentially serve as the 'illah for a ruling.
دليل التمييز (dalīl al-tamyīz): Evidence that distinguishes the specific 'illah from other potential attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is required before using an attribute from a text as an 'illah in qiyas?
A) That the attribute be a possible cause and no preventing factor exists.
B) That the text itself be from the Qur'an or Sunnah.
C) That a distinguishing evidence (dalīl al-tamyīz) be established to show the text is caused and which attribute is the 'illah.
D) That the attribute be mentioned explicitly in a hadith.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ta'lil requires a distinguishing evidence (dalīl al-tamyīz) to identify the 'illah; not all attributes are automatically valid causes.
